## Publisher content schema

This is what publisher apps send to the publishing-api.

[Schema on GitHub](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/alphagov/govuk-content-schemas/master/dist/formats/html_publication/publisher_v2/schema.json)

<table class='schema-table'><tr><td><strong>access_limited</strong> <code>object</code></td> <td><table class='schema-table'><tr><td><strong>users</strong> <code>array</code></td> <td></td></tr></table></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>analytics_identifier</strong> <code>string</code> or <code>null</code></td> <td>A short identifier we send to Google Analytics for multi-valued fields. This means we avoid the truncated values we would get if we sent the path or slug of eg organisations.</td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>base_path</strong> <code>string</code></td> <td>A path only. Query string and/or fragment are not allowed.</td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>description</strong> <code>string</code> or <code>null</code></td> <td></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>details</strong> <code>object</code></td> <td><table class='schema-table'><tr><td><strong>body</strong> <code>string</code></td> <td></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>headings</strong> <code>string</code></td> <td></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>public_timestamp</strong> <code>string</code></td> <td></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>first_published_version</strong> <code>boolean</code></td> <td></td></tr></table></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>document_type</strong> <code>string</code></td> <td></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>first_published_at</strong> <code>string</code></td> <td></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>last_edited_at</strong> <code>string</code></td> <td>Last time when the content recieved a major or minor update.</td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>locale</strong> <code>string</code></td> <td>Allowed values: <code>ar</code> or <code>az</code> or <code>be</code> or <code>bg</code> or <code>bn</code> or <code>cs</code> or <code>cy</code> or <code>de</code> or <code>dr</code> or <code>el</code> or <code>en</code> or <code>es</code> or <code>es-419</code> or <code>et</code> or <code>fa</code> or <code>fr</code> or <code>he</code> or <code>hi</code> or <code>hu</code> or <code>hy</code> or <code>id</code> or <code>it</code> or <code>ja</code> or <code>ka</code> or <code>ko</code> or <code>lt</code> or <code>lv</code> or <code>ms</code> or <code>pl</code> or <code>ps</code> or <code>pt</code> or <code>ro</code> or <code>ru</code> or <code>si</code> or <code>sk</code> or <code>so</code> or <code>sq</code> or <code>sr</code> or <code>sw</code> or <code>ta</code> or <code>th</code> or <code>tk</code> or <code>tr</code> or <code>uk</code> or <code>ur</code> or <code>uz</code> or <code>vi</code> or <code>zh</code> or <code>zh-hk</code> or <code>zh-tw</code></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>need_ids</strong> <code>array</code></td> <td></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>phase</strong> <code>string</code></td> <td>Allowed values: <code>alpha</code> or <code>beta</code> or <code>live</code>The service design phase of this content item - https://www.gov.uk/service-manual/phases</td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>previous_version</strong> <code>string</code></td> <td></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>public_updated_at</strong> <code>string</code></td> <td></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>publishing_app</strong> <code>string</code></td> <td></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>redirects</strong> <code>array</code></td> <td></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>rendering_app</strong> <code>string</code></td> <td></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>routes</strong> <code>array</code></td> <td></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>schema_name</strong> <code>string</code></td> <td>Allowed values: <code>html_publication</code></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>title</strong> <code>string</code></td> <td></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>update_type</strong> </td> <td>Allowed values: <code>major</code> or <code>minor</code> or <code>republish</code></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>withdrawn_notice</strong> <code>object</code></td> <td><table class='schema-table'><tr><td><strong>explanation</strong> <code>string</code></td> <td></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>withdrawn_at</strong> </td> <td></td></tr></table></td></tr></table>



---

## Publisher links schema

The links for this item.

[Schema on GitHub](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/alphagov/govuk-content-schemas/master/dist/formats/html_publication/publisher_v2/links.json)

<table class='schema-table'><tr><td><strong>links</strong> <code>object</code></td> <td><table class='schema-table'><tr><td><strong>taxons</strong> </td> <td>Prototype-stage taxonomy label for this content item</td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>mainstream_browse_pages</strong> </td> <td>Powers the /browse section of the site. These are known as sections in some legacy apps.</td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>topics</strong> </td> <td>Powers the /topic section of the site. These are known as specialist sectors in some legacy apps.</td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>organisations</strong> </td> <td>All organisations linked to this content item. This should include lead organisations.</td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>parent</strong> </td> <td>The parent content item.</td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>policies</strong> </td> <td>These are for collecting content related to a particular government policy.</td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>policy_areas</strong> </td> <td>A largely deprecated tag currently only used to power email alerts.</td></tr></table></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>previous_version</strong> <code>string</code></td> <td></td></tr></table>

---

## Frontend schema

This is the schema for what you'll get back from the content-store.

[Schema on GitHub](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/alphagov/govuk-content-schemas/master/dist/formats/html_publication/frontend/schema.json)

<table class='schema-table'><tr><td><strong>analytics_identifier</strong> <code>string</code> or <code>null</code></td> <td>A short identifier we send to Google Analytics for multi-valued fields. This means we avoid the truncated values we would get if we sent the path or slug of eg organisations.</td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>base_path</strong> <code>string</code></td> <td>A path only. Query string and/or fragment are not allowed.</td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>content_id</strong> <code>string</code></td> <td></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>description</strong> <code>string</code> or <code>null</code></td> <td></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>details</strong> <code>object</code></td> <td><table class='schema-table'><tr><td><strong>body</strong> <code>string</code></td> <td></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>headings</strong> <code>string</code></td> <td></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>public_timestamp</strong> <code>string</code></td> <td></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>first_published_version</strong> <code>boolean</code></td> <td></td></tr></table></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>document_type</strong> <code>string</code></td> <td></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>expanded_links</strong> <code>object</code></td> <td></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>first_published_at</strong> <code>string</code></td> <td></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>format</strong> <code>string</code></td> <td></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>last_edited_at</strong> <code>string</code></td> <td>Last time when the content recieved a major or minor update.</td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>links</strong> <code>object</code></td> <td><table class='schema-table'><tr><td><strong>taxons</strong> </td> <td></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>mainstream_browse_pages</strong> </td> <td></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>topics</strong> </td> <td></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>organisations</strong> </td> <td></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>parent</strong> </td> <td></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>policies</strong> </td> <td></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>policy_areas</strong> </td> <td></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>available_translations</strong> </td> <td></td></tr></table></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>locale</strong> <code>string</code></td> <td>Allowed values: <code>ar</code> or <code>az</code> or <code>be</code> or <code>bg</code> or <code>bn</code> or <code>cs</code> or <code>cy</code> or <code>de</code> or <code>dr</code> or <code>el</code> or <code>en</code> or <code>es</code> or <code>es-419</code> or <code>et</code> or <code>fa</code> or <code>fr</code> or <code>he</code> or <code>hi</code> or <code>hu</code> or <code>hy</code> or <code>id</code> or <code>it</code> or <code>ja</code> or <code>ka</code> or <code>ko</code> or <code>lt</code> or <code>lv</code> or <code>ms</code> or <code>pl</code> or <code>ps</code> or <code>pt</code> or <code>ro</code> or <code>ru</code> or <code>si</code> or <code>sk</code> or <code>so</code> or <code>sq</code> or <code>sr</code> or <code>sw</code> or <code>ta</code> or <code>th</code> or <code>tk</code> or <code>tr</code> or <code>uk</code> or <code>ur</code> or <code>uz</code> or <code>vi</code> or <code>zh</code> or <code>zh-hk</code> or <code>zh-tw</code></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>need_ids</strong> <code>array</code></td> <td></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>phase</strong> <code>string</code></td> <td>Allowed values: <code>alpha</code> or <code>beta</code> or <code>live</code>The service design phase of this content item - https://www.gov.uk/service-manual/phases</td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>public_updated_at</strong> <code>string</code></td> <td></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>publishing_app</strong> <code>string</code></td> <td></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>rendering_app</strong> <code>string</code></td> <td></td></tr>
<tr><td><strong>schema_name</strong> <code>string</code></td> <td>Allowed values: <code>html_publication</code></td></tr>

## Frontend examples


### arabic_translation.json
```json
{
  "content_id": "1d0ba5bd-8a0a-41a7-950a-c7b819da6336",
  "base_path": "/government/publications/why-overseas-companies-should-set-up-in-the-uk/1156044",
  "details": {
    "body": "<div class=\"govspeak\"><h2>\n<span class=\"number\">1. </span>الوجهة الأولى في أوروبا للاستثمار الوارد</h2>\n\n<p><a rel=\"external\" href=\"http://youtu.be/drhpxS5lJbg\">Why companies invest in the UK</a></p>\n\n<p>الشركات التي تؤسس أعمالها في المملكة المتحدة عددها أكبر من تلك التي تؤسس أعمالها في أي دولة أخرى في أوروبا.</p>\n\n<p>تختار شركات دولية تأسيس أعمالها في المملكة المتحدة لأنها تريد:</p>\n\n<ul>\n  <li>الوصول لعملاء جدد وحاليين</li>\n  <li>تطوير منتجات جديدة</li>\n  <li>البحث عن موردين وشركاء جدد</li>\n  <li>إقامة مزيد من علاقات العمل بدول أخرى في أنحاء أوروبا</li>\n</ul>\n\n<p>باستطاعة الشركات التي مقرها في المملكة المتحدة الوصول إلى أكثر من 500 مليون من العملاء في أنحاء أوروبا.</p>\n\n<p>كما أنها لا تدفع أي رسوم عن الاستيراد أو التصدير ضمن الاتحاد الأوروبي. وتوجد أيضا اتفاقيات للتجارة الحرة أو المحترفة بين المملكة المتحدة والكثير من الدول من خارج الاتحاد الأوروبي. </p>\n\n<p>ومن الأسهل كذلك إقامة علاقات عمل في المملكة المتحدة مقارنة بغيرها من الدول الأوروبية الكبرى. </p>\n\n<div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<p><a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/government/publications/ukti-inward-investment-report-2014-to-2015\">إقرأ تقرير الاستثمار الوارد إلى المملكة المتحدة عن العام 2014 إلى 2015.</a></p>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<p><a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/government/publications/invest-in-the-uk-your-springboard-for-global-growth\">إقرأ المقارنة بين المملكة المتحدة والدول الأخرى كوجهة جاذبة للاستثمار. </a></p>\n</div>\n\n<figure class=\"image embedded\">\n  <div class=\"img\"><img alt=\"Infographic: It's easy to do business in the UK\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/uploads/system/uploads/image_data/file/38468/Info_3.jpg\"></div>\n  <figcaption>Infographic: It's easy to do business in the UK</figcaption>\n</figure>\n<p> \n##ما تقوله شركات دولية عن المملكة المتحدة </p>\n\n<h3 id=\"section-1\">\n<span class=\"number\">1.1 </span>خمس من المستثمرين الدوليين الكبار يتحدثون عن سبب كون المملكة المتحدة مكانا رائعا لإقامة علاقات العمل فيها.</h3>\n\n<p><a rel=\"external\" href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=SsO6pYJ0ZGc&amp;list=PLW9Q9i8L1YhWmK5TCSHxSWsWW9YuKmnvz\">Investment video</a>\n \n##فرص في قطاعات مختلفة </p>\n\n<p>اكتشف فرص الاستثمار في قطاعات محددة، من بينها:</p>\n\n<ul>\n  <li><a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/government/publications/aerospace-industry-in-the-uk-investment-opportunities\">الطائرات والطيران</a></li>\n  <li><a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/government/publications/agri-tech-in-the-uk-investment-opportunities\">التقنية الزراعية</a></li>\n  <li><a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/government/publications/automotive-industry-in-the-uk-investment-opportunities\">السيارات ومحركاتها</a></li>\n  <li><a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/government/publications/communications-industry-in-the-uk-investment-opportunities\">الاتصالات</a></li>\n  <li><a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/government/publications/civil-nuclear-power-in-the-uk-investment-opportunities\">الطاقة النووية للاستخدامات المدنية</a></li>\n  <li><a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/government/publications/creative-industries-in-the-uk-investment-opportunities\">الصناعات المبدعة</a></li>\n  <li><a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/government/publications/electronics-and-it-hardware-in-the-uk-investment-opportunities\">الإلكترونيات وأجهزة تكنولوجيا المعلومات</a></li>\n  <li><a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/government/publications/energy-networks-in-the-uk-investment-opportunities\">شبكات الطاقة</a></li>\n  <li><a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/ukti/fso\">الخدمات المالية</a></li>\n  <li><a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/government/publications/food-and-drink-in-the-uk-investment-opportunities\">المأكولات والمشروبات</a></li>\n  <li><a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/government/publications/information-communications-technology-ict-in-the-uk-investment-opportunities\">تكنولوجيا المعلومات والاتصالات</a></li>\n  <li><a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/ukti/lso\">علوم الحياة</a></li>\n  <li><a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/government/publications/offshore-wind-power-in-the-uk-investment-opportunities\">الطاقة الهوائية في عرض البحر</a></li>\n  <li><a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/government/publications/oil-and-gas-in-the-uk-investment-opportunities\">النفط والغاز</a></li>\n  <li><a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/government/publications/marine-energy-in-the-uk-investment-opportunities\">الطاقة البحرية</a></li>\n  <li><a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/government/publications/rail-industry-guide-for-overseas-investors\">السكك الحديدية</a></li>\n  <li><a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/government/publications/retail-sector-in-the-uk-investment-opportunities\">تجارة التجزئة</a></li>\n  <li><a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/ukti/rio\">تجديد المناطق (بنية تحتية)</a></li>\n  <li><a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/government/publications/space-technology-in-the-uk-investment-opportunities\">تكنولوجيا الفضاء</a></li>\n  <li><a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/government/publications/waste-management-in-the-uk-investment-opportunities\">إدارة النفايات</a></li>\n</ul>\n\n<h2 id=\"section-2\">\n<span class=\"number\">2. </span>الضرائب في المملكة المتحدة</h2>\n\n<h3 id=\"section-3\">\n<span class=\"number\">2.1 </span>نسبة ضريبة الشركات 20%</h3>\n\n<p>النسبة <a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/corporation-tax\">الحالية لضرائب الشركات</a> هي 20%، وهي بذلك أقل نسبة مشتركة في دول مجموعة العشرين - أكبر 20 اقتصادا في العالم.</p>\n\n<p>وقد وقعت المملكة المتحدة اتفاقيات لتجنب الازدواج الضريبي مع دول أخرى. وأغلب الشركات العاملة في المملكة المتحدة لا تدفع ضرائب عن الفوائد التي تحققها في الخارج. </p>\n\n<div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<p><a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/government/collections/tax-treaties-signed-and-in-force\">المزيد عن الاتفاقيات الضريبية الموقعة بين المملكة المتحدة ودول أخرى</a></p>\n</div>\n\n<p> \n##المهارات والتوظيف</p>\n\n<figure class=\"image embedded\">\n  <div class=\"img\"><img alt=\"Infographic: The UK has the 2nd largest labour force in the EU\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/uploads/system/uploads/image_data/file/38467/Info_2.jpg\"></div>\n  <figcaption>Infographic: The UK has the 2nd largest labour force in the UK</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\n<p>تتوفر في المملكة المتحدة قوى عاملة يبلغ قوامها 30 مليون شخص، وبذلك لديها ثاني أكبر قوى عاملة في الاتحاد الأوروبي. </p>\n\n<p>ونحن واحدة من دول أوروبية قليلة يتوقع لها أن تشهد نموا في توفر القوى العاملة على مدى 15 سنة القادمة. </p>\n\n<p>لدى المملكة المتحدة: </p>\n\n<ul>\n  <li>قوى عاملة تتمتع بمهارات عالية</li>\n  <li>سوق عمل مرنة</li>\n  <li>تنظيمات وضعت لحماية الموظفين</li>\n</ul>\n\n<p>وقوانين العمل المرنة لدينا تعني أن باستطاعة الشركات تعيين موظفين وفق ما يناسب احتياجات أعمالها. </p>\n\n<p>هذا إلى جانب أن تكاليف العمالة في المملكة المتحدة هي من بين الأكثر تنافسا في غرب أوروبا، وما يساهم بذلك هو انخفاض ما تدفعه الشركات من ضمان اجتماعي. </p>\n\n<p>كما التكاليف العامة للعمالة في المملكة المتحدة أقل مما هي في دول أخرى مثل فرنسا وأيرلندا وهولندا وألمانيا. </p>\n\n<div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<p><a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/browse/employing-people\">دليل توظيف العمالة في المملكة المتحدة </a></p>\n</div>\n\n<p>إن كنت ترغب بتعيين موظفين، باستطاعة شبكة مراكز العمل مساعدتك. حيث أنها تقدم خدمة مجانية تشمل تقديم المشورة بشأن: </p>\n\n<ul>\n  <li>طرق وإجراءات التوظيف</li>\n  <li>توفر مرشحين مناسبين للعمل</li>\n  <li>الإعلان عن توفر شواغر العمل</li>\n  <li>ملء شواغر العمل</li>\n  <li>تعيين موظفين ذوي إعاقة</li>\n</ul>\n\n<h2 id=\"section-4\">\n<span class=\"number\">3. </span>الحصول على مساعدة من الهيئة البريطانية للتجارة والاستثمار</h2>\n\n<p>باستطاعة الهيئة البريطانية للتجارة والاستثمار مساعدة الشركات الأجنبية التي تتطلع إلى تأسيس الأعمال أو الاستثمار في المملكة المتحدة عن طريق تقديم عدد من الخدمات المجانية لهذه الشركات. من بين الخدمات ما يلي:</p>\n\n<ul>\n  <li>تحديد الفرص المتوفرة في أسواق المملكة المتحدة وأوروبا</li>\n  <li>وضع الشركات على اتصال بالأشخاص المناسبين وتقديمها لهم </li>\n  <li>تأسيس العمل في المملكة المتحدة </li>\n  <li>أبحاث السوق</li>\n  <li>اختيار أفضل مقر</li>\n  <li>نصائح ضريبية</li>\n  <li>مساندة حكومية مستمرة بعد تأسيس عملك في المملكة المتحدة </li>\n  <li>تقديم طلب التأشيرة ودخول المملكة المتحدة </li>\n  <li>إيجاد موظفين</li>\n  <li>دعم لرواد الأعمال </li>\n</ul>\n\n<p>باستطاعة الهيئة البريطانية للتجارة والاستثمار أن تقدم للشركات والمستثمرين من الخارج مزيدا من المعلومات حول تأسيس أعمالهم في المملكة المتحدة. </p>\n\n<div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>الاستفسارات من الشركات الأجنبية الراغبة بتأسيس أعمالها في المملكة المتحدة</h4>\n\n<table>\n  <tbody>\n    <tr>\n      <td>البريد الإلكتروني</td>\n      <td><a href=\"mailto:enquiries@ukti-invest.com\">enquiries@ukti-invest.com</a></td>\n    </tr>\n  </tbody>\n</table>\n\n<table>\n  <tbody>\n    <tr>\n      <td>نموذج الاتصال</td>\n      <td><a rel=\"external\" href=\"https://www.contactus.ukti.gov.uk/uktihome/contactus/investmentcontactusform.html\">https://www.contactus.ukti.gov.uk….</a></td>\n    </tr>\n  </tbody>\n</table>\n\n<table>\n  <tbody>\n    <tr>\n      <td>الاتصال هاتفيا (من خارج المملكة المتحدة)</td>\n      <td>+44 (0)20 7333 5442</td>\n    </tr>\n  </tbody>\n</table>\n\n<table>\n  <tbody>\n    <tr>\n      <td>الاتصال هاتفيا (من داخل المملكة المتحدة)</td>\n      <td>0845 539 0419</td>\n    </tr>\n  </tbody>\n</table>\n\n<p>باستطاعة الشركات الأجنبية الاتصال بفريق خدمات الاستثمار لدى الهيئة البريطانية للتجارة والاستثمار للحصول على معلومات بشأن تأسيس أعمالها في المملكة المتحدة، ومعرفة أنواع المساعدة المتوفرة لها.</p>\n</div>\n\n<p> \n##تطوير البنية التحتية في المملكة المتحدة </p>\n\n<p>إن وجود بنية تحتية قوية مهم للمساعدة في نمو الأعمال. </p>\n\n<p>توجد مشاريع بنية تحتية كبيرة بمجال: </p>\n\n<ul>\n  <li>الطاقة</li>\n  <li>النقل</li>\n  <li>إدارة النفايات</li>\n  <li>السيطرة على الفيضانات</li>\n  <li>العلوم</li>\n  <li>المياه</li>\n  <li>الاتصالات </li>\n</ul>\n\n<h3 id=\"section-5\">\n<span class=\"number\">3.1 </span>تحسين وسائل النقل</h3>\n\n<p>يساعد برنامج استثماري يبلغ 120 مليار جنيه استرليني في تحسين أنظمة النقل. </p>\n\n<p>ولدى المملكة المتحدة بالفعل: </p>\n\n<ul>\n  <li>ثاني أكبر قطاع موانئ في أوروبا</li>\n  <li>أكبر نظام للنقل الجوي في أوروبا</li>\n  <li>شبكة حديدية أفضل تطورا في الاتحاد الأوروبي </li>\n</ul>\n\n<p>ولدينا برنامج استثماري مدته 7 سنوات لتحسين الطرقات في المملكة المتحدة بهدف تسهيل نقل البضائع والمسافرين من وإلى المملكة المتحدة. </p>\n\n<p>ومن بين مشاريع السكك الحديدية الكبيرة لدينا: </p>\n\n<h4 id=\"crossrail\">كروسريل - Crossrail</h4>\n\n<p>سوف تساعد هذه الشبكة الحديدية الجديدة التي تربط شرق وغرب لندن في تقليل الوقت الذي يستغرقه 1.5 مليون مسافر إضافي للوصول إلى وسط لندن إلى 45 دقيقة. </p>\n\n<h4 id=\"high-speed-2\">هاي سبيد 2 – High Speed 2</h4>\n\n<p>شبكة سكة حديدية سريعة تربط بين ثمانية من بين أكبر عشر مدن في بريطانيا، وتخدم واحدا من بين كل خمس من السكان.</p>\n\n<div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<p><a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/government/organisations/infrastructure-uk\">إقرأ المزيد عن تطوير البنية التحتية في المملكة المتحدة </a></p>\n</div>\n\n<p> \n##رواد الأعمال والخريجون الجدد </p>\n\n<p>ترحب المملكة المتحدة برواد الأعمال وبمن يرغبون بتأسيس أعمالهم الخاصة. </p>\n\n<p>وتقدم المملكة المتحدة، من خلال برنامج رواد الأعمال، دعما لرواد الأعمال المؤهلين وفق المعايير التالية:</p>\n\n<ul>\n  <li>\n<a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/government/publications/entrepreneurs-setting-up-in-the-uk/entrepreneurs-setting-up-in-the-uk\">البرنامج العالمي لرواد الأعمال</a>  – المخصص لرواد أعمال أو شركات في المراحل الأولى من التأسيس</li>\n  <li>\n<a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/government/collections/sirius-programme-for-graduate-entrepreneurs\">برنامج سيريوس</a> – المخصص للطلاب في السنة النهائية من دراستهم الجامعية أو للخريجين الجدد ممن بدأوا مشاريع عمل جديدة أو لديهم أفكار عمل جديدة</li>\n</ul>\n\n<h2 id=\"section-6\">\n<span class=\"number\">4. </span>التصدير من المملكة المتحدة</h2>\n\n<p>عندما تؤسس عملك في المملكة المتحدة يمكنك <a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/government/collections/uk-trade-and-investment-services-for-exporters\">الاستفادة من نفس الدعم</a>  لزيادة الصادرات المقدم للشركات البريطانية. \n \n##إيجاد مقر لشركتك </p>\n\n<p>يمكنك استئجار أو شراء مقر تجاري أو صناعي في أي مكان في المملكة المتحدة. </p>\n\n<p>بعض النشاطات التجارية تتطلب الحصول على موافقة محددة، ويمكن أن يكون مسموح بها في مواقع محددة فقط. </p>\n\n<p>وإن كنت ترغب ببناء أو توسيع مبنى، فإن عملية الحصول على الموافقة على ذلك بسيطة. </p>\n\n<p>ويقول البنك الدولي بأن عملية الحصول على إذن بالبناء والموافقة على النشاط في المملكة المتحدة هي من بين الأسهل في الاتحاد الأوروبي، وأفضل مما هي في سويسرا وهولندا وفرنسا وأيرلندا. </p>\n\n<h3 id=\"section-7\">\n<span class=\"number\">4.1 </span>مناطق الأعمال</h3>\n\n<p>مناطق الأعمال هي مواقع منتشرة في أنحاء المملكة المتحدة توفر للشركات الحوافز لتأسيس مقراتها فيها. </p>\n\n<p>من بين الحوافز: </p>\n\n<ul>\n  <li>ضرائب أقل</li>\n  <li>قواعد أبسط للموافقة على الخطط </li>\n  <li>مزايا مادية</li>\n</ul>\n\n<p>وتتوفر في الكثير من مناطق الأعمال تجمعات لفرص العمل، حيث تتجمع شركات من نفس القطاع في نفس المنطقة. </p>\n\n<p>مزيد من المعلومات حول مناطق الأعمال في <a rel=\"external\" href=\"https://www.localinvestuk.com/about/about-enterprise-zones\">إنجلترا</a> و<a rel=\"external\" href=\"http://business.wales.gov.uk/enterprisezones\">ويلز</a>  و<a rel=\"external\" href=\"http://www.sdi.co.uk/knowledge-hub/articles/insight/scotlands-enterprise-areas\">اسكتلندا</a>. \n \n##تسجيل شركة في المملكة المتحدة </p>\n\n<p>إن كنت بصدد تأسيس عمل في المملكة المتحدة، عليك <a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/register-as-an-overseas-company\">التسجيل لدى سجل الشركات</a>.</p>\n\n<p>هناك قواعد تتعلق باستخدام أسماء الشركات. وبعض القطاعات، كالخدمات المالية والدفاع والتنقيب عن النفط، قد تتطلب الحصول على إذن أو ترخيص. </p>\n\n<p>إن أردت تأسيس شركة جديدة ذات مسؤولية محدودة في المملكة المتحدة، عليك التسجيل لدى سجل الشركات. ذلك يكلف 20 جنيها استرلينيا وتستغرق عملية التسجيل نحو 24 ساعة. </p>\n\n<p>ليس بالإمكان تسجيل الشراكات والكيانات التي لا تكون منطوية تحت شركة على أنها شركات أجنبية في المملكة المتحدة. \n \n##التأشيرات والهجرة </p>\n\n<p>هناك عدد من التأشيرات البريطانية المختلفة، وهي تعتمد على ظروفك. من بين هذه التأشيرات: </p>\n\n<ul>\n  <li>\n<a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/tier-1-investor\">تأشيرة مستثمر</a> </li>\n  <li><a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/tier-1-entrepreneur\">تأشيرة رائد أعمال</a></li>\n  <li><a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/tier-1-graduate-entrepreneur-visa\">تأشيرة رائد أعمال حديث التخرج من الجامعة</a></li>\n  <li><a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/representative-overseas-business/overview\">تأشيرة ممثل لشركة أجنبية</a></li>\n  <li><a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/tier-2-general/overview\">تأشيرة عامة</a></li>\n</ul>\n\n<div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<p><a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/check-uk-visa\">يرجى التحقق مما إذا كنت بحاجة لتأشيرة للحضور إلى المملكة المتحدة</a></p>\n</div>\n\n<p> \n##المساعدة المالية </p>\n\n<p>يمكن للشركات الحصول على منح والاستفادة من إعفاءات ضريبية في المملكة المتحدة. وبذلك تتوفر لها مساعدة مالية بمجالات الأبحاث والتطوير والاستثمار في الشركات. </p>\n\n<h3 id=\"section-8\">\n<span class=\"number\">4.2 </span>فرص التمويل</h3>\n\n<p>الشركات في المملكة المتحدة قد تكون مؤهلة للاستفادة من مساعدات مالية محلية ومن الاتحاد الأوروبي تشمل: </p>\n\n<ul>\n  <li>منح حكومية</li>\n  <li>تمويل وقروض</li>\n  <li>دعم لنشاط الشركة</li>\n  <li>تمويل لبدء النشاط التجاري أو للشركات الصغيرة والمتوسطة</li>\n</ul>\n\n<div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<p><a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/business-finance-support-finder\">يمكنك البحث في البرامج التي تستفيد من التمويل العام</a>  في المملكة المتحدة</p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"section-9\">\n<span class=\"number\">4.3 </span>تمويل النمو في مناطق المملكة المتحدة</h3>\n\n<p>يدعم <a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/understanding-the-regional-growth-fund#overview\">صندوق النمو في المناطق</a>  المشاريع والبرامج التي تستعين باستثمارات القطاع الخاص لتحقيق النمو الاقتصادي وتوفير فرص العمل بمناطق مختلفة في المملكة المتحدة. </p>\n\n<h3 id=\"section-10\">\n<span class=\"number\">4.4 </span>المستثمرون الممولون لرواد الأعمال</h3>\n\n<p>هم عبارة عن أفراد أو جماعات لديهم إمكانية توفير رأس المال لبدء نشاط جديد أو مساندة نشاط شركة في مراحله المبكرة. </p>\n\n<p>يستخدم المستثمرون الممولون لرواد الأعمال أموالهم الخاصة أو شركاتهم أو خبراتهم المهنية للاستثمار في نمو شركات صغيرة. </p>\n\n<div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<p><a rel=\"external\" href=\"http://www.ukbusinessangelsassociation.org.uk\">ابحث عن مستثمرين ممولين لرواد الأعمال في المملكة المتحدة </a></p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"section-11\">\n<span class=\"number\">4.5 </span>الأسهم الخاصة ورأس المال الاستثماري</h3>\n\n<p>شركات الأسهم الخاصة تستحوذ في بعض الأحيان على حصة الأغلبية في الشركات التي يُنتظر أن تحقق نموا كبيرا. </p>\n\n<p>ومؤسسات رأس المال الاستثماري تستثمر في أسهم الشركات التي يُنتظر أن تحقق نموا كبيرا، وهي شركات عادة ما تكون في مرحلة التأسيس أو بدء النشاط أو المراحل المبكرة من النمو. </p>\n\n<div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<p><a rel=\"external\" href=\"http://www.bvca.co.uk\">ابحث عن المؤسسات البريطانية المختصة بالأسهم الخاصة ومؤسسات رأس المال الاستثماري</a></p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"section-12\">\n<span class=\"number\">4.6 </span>المنح</h3>\n\n<p>المنح هي أموال تقدم لأفراد أو شركات لمساندة غرض أو مشروع معين. </p>\n\n<p>يتعين عادة استيفاء معايير محددة، من بينها: </p>\n\n<ul>\n  <li>موقع الشخص مقدم الطلب</li>\n  <li>كيفية إنفاق المنحة</li>\n  <li>التغيير الذي يمكن أن يتحقق بفضل المنحة</li>\n</ul>\n\n<div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<p><a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/business-finance-explained/grants\">المزيد عن المنح</a></p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"section-13\">\n<span class=\"number\">4.7 </span>قروض لبدء النشاط التجاري</h3>\n\n<p>باستطاعة الشركات التي مضى على تأسيسها أقل من 12 شهرا الحصول على مساعدة في الترتيب لأخذ قرض لبدء نشاطها. </p>\n\n<p>وباستطاعة <a rel=\"external\" href=\"http://british-business-bank.co.uk/\">بنك الأعمال البريطاني</a>  مساعدة رواد الأعمال الذين ليس باستطاعتهم الحصول على تمويل من البنوك. </p>\n\n<p>هذا البنك معني بالتنمية الاقتصادية ومدعوم من الحكومة، وهو يدير 3.9 مليون جنيه استرليني من أموال الحكومة المخصصة لتوفير أسواق مال فعالة لمساعدة الشركات الأصغر حجما. </p>\n\n<p>يعمل بنك الأعمال البريطاني مع أكثر من 70 جهة شريكة، وهو يستخدم التمويل الحكومي ويستعين بضمانات موجهة لتشجيع القطاع الخاص على زيادة الإقراض والاستثمار. </p>\n\n<p>وقد استفادت 25,000 شركة بريطانية من حلول قدمها بنك الأعمال مع نهاية عام 2013. \n \n##حقوق الملكية الفكرية </p>\n\n<p><a rel=\"external\" href=\"http://www.ipo.gov.uk/\">مكتب الملكية الفكرية</a>  معني بحقوق الملكية الفكرية، وهو بالتالي يكفل الالتزام بالاتفاقيات الدولية لحماية هذه الحقوق. </p>\n\n<h3 id=\"section-14\">\n<span class=\"number\">4.8 </span>البراءات وعلامات الاختراع</h3>\n\n<p>البراءة تحمي الاختراعات، وهي تشمل: </p>\n\n<ul>\n  <li>كيفية عمل الأشياء</li>\n  <li>ما تفعله الأشياء</li>\n  <li>كيف تفعله</li>\n  <li>المواد المستخدم في صناعتها</li>\n  <li>كيفية صناعتها</li>\n</ul>\n\n<p>والعلامة التجارية هي رمز يميز بضائع وخدمات شركة ما عن غيرها من الشركات.</p>\n\n<p>العلامة التجارية يمكن أن تكون: </p>\n\n<ul>\n  <li>كلمات</li>\n  <li>شعارات</li>\n  <li>صور</li>\n  <li>أصوات</li>\n</ul>\n\n<p>وهناك 45 نوعا (درجة) من نشاطات الشركات في المملكة المتحدة يمكن تسجيل العلامات التجارية بموجبها. </p>\n\n<p>تكلفة <a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/register-a-trademark\">تسجيل علامة تجارية</a> :</p>\n\n<ul>\n  <li>170 جنيها استرلينيا للتسجيل عبر الإنترنت</li>\n  <li>200 جنيه استرليني لتقديم طلب خطي</li>\n  <li>50 جنيها استرلينيا إضافيا لكل نوع نشاط تجاري يضاف للطلب </li>\n</ul>\n\n<p>باستطاعة الشركات تقديم الطلب بنفسها أو الاستعانة بمستشار للعلامات التجارية. </p>\n\n<div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<p><a rel=\"external\" href=\"http://www.itma.org.uk\">ابحث عن مستشار للعلامات التجارية</a></p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"section-15\">\n<span class=\"number\">4.9 </span>حقوق الطبع</h3>\n\n<p>لست بحاجة للتسجيل لحقوق الطبع في المملكة المتحدة. حيث أن أي مادة تصبح محمية بحقوق الطبع بمجرد كتابتها أو تسجيلها. وهذا يشمل: </p>\n\n<ul>\n  <li>الفنون</li>\n  <li>مواد البث</li>\n  <li>برامج الحاسوب</li>\n  <li>قواعد البيانات</li>\n  <li>الأفلام</li>\n  <li>المواد الأدبية</li>\n  <li>الموسيقى</li>\n  <li>الصور</li>\n  <li>الرسومات الفنية</li>\n  <li>المواقع الإلكترونية</li>\n</ul>\n\n<p>وعملك المحمي بحقوق الطبع يخضع لنفس الحماية في الخارج كما هو محمي في المملكة المتحدة. </p>\n\n<h3 id=\"section-16\">\n<span class=\"number\">4.10 </span>التصميم</h3>\n\n<p>يصف التصميم مظهر أو شكل منتجات مصنعة. </p>\n\n<p>والقانون يشمل نوعين من الحماية:</p>\n\n<ol>\n  <li>مسجلة: ينظر مكتب الملكية الفكرية في المملكة المتحدة وغيره من المؤسسات الدولية في التصاميم ويسجلها بمقابل رسم</li>\n  <li>غير مسجلة: حقوق التصميم تكون تلقائية لكنها توفر حماية أقل</li>\n</ol>\n\n<h3 id=\"section-17\">\n<span class=\"number\">4.11 </span>تنظيمات تتعلق بقطاعات محددة</h3>\n\n<p>هناك <a rel=\"external\" href=\"http://www.ipo.gov.uk/business\">تنظيمات وحمايات محددة</a>  في مجالات محددة من القطاعات التخصصية. وفي هذه الحالة يمكن أن تكون حقوق الملكية الفكرية معقدة، ويتعين على الشركات المعنية السعي للحصول على مشورة من جهة محترفة. </p>\n</div>",
    "headings": "<ol><li><a href=\"#section\">الوجهة الأولى في أوروبا للاستثمار الوارد</a></li><li><a href=\"#section-2\">الضرائب في المملكة المتحدة</a></li><li><a href=\"#section-4\">الحصول على مساعدة من الهيئة البريطانية للتجارة والاستثمار</a></li><li><a href=\"#section-6\">التصدير من المملكة المتحدة</a></li></ol>",
```

### fractions_and_unnumbered_headings.json
```json
{
  "content_id": "1d0ba5bd-8a0a-41a7-950a-c7b819da6336",
  "base_path": "/government/publications/national-curriculum-in-england-mathematics-programmes-of-study/national-curriculum-in-england-mathematics-programmes-of-study",
  "details": {
    "body": "<div class=\"govspeak\"><h3 id=\"purpose-of-study\">Purpose of study</h3>\n\n<p>Mathematics is a creative and highly interconnected discipline that has been developed over centuries, providing the solution to some of history’s most intriguing problems. It is essential to everyday life, critical to science, technology and engineering, and necessary for financial literacy and most forms of employment. A high-quality mathematics education therefore provides a foundation for understanding the world, the ability to reason mathematically, an appreciation of the beauty and power of mathematics, and a sense of enjoyment and curiosity about the subject.</p>\n\n<h3 id=\"aims\">Aims</h3>\n\n<p>The national curriculum for mathematics aims to ensure that all pupils:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>become fluent in the fundamentals of mathematics, including through varied and frequent practice with increasingly complex problems over time, so that pupils develop conceptual understanding and the ability to recall and apply knowledge rapidly and accurately</li>\n  <li>reason mathematically by following a line of enquiry, conjecturing relationships and generalisations, and developing an argument, justification or proof using mathematical language</li>\n  <li>can solve problems by applying their mathematics to a variety of routine and non-routine problems with increasing sophistication, including breaking down problems into a series of simpler steps and persevering in seeking solutions</li>\n</ul><p>Mathematics is an interconnected subject in which pupils need to be able to move fluently between representations of mathematical ideas. The programmes of study are, by necessity, organised into apparently distinct domains, but pupils should make rich connections across mathematical ideas to develop fluency, mathematical reasoning and competence in solving increasingly sophisticated problems. They should also apply their mathematical knowledge to science and other subjects.</p>\n\n<p>The expectation is that the majority of pupils will move through the programmes of study at broadly the same pace. However, decisions about when to progress should always be based on the security of pupils’ understanding and their readiness to progress to the next stage. Pupils who grasp concepts rapidly should be challenged through being offered rich and sophisticated problems before any acceleration through new content. Those who are not sufficiently fluent with earlier material should consolidate their understanding, including through additional practice, before moving on.</p>\n\n<h3 id=\"information-and-communication-technology-ict\">Information and communication technology (ICT)</h3>\n\n<p>Calculators should not be used as a substitute for good written and mental arithmetic. They should therefore only be introduced near the end of key stage 2 to support pupils’ conceptual understanding and exploration of more complex number problems, if written and mental arithmetic are secure. In both primary and secondary schools, teachers should use their judgement about when ICT tools should be used.</p>\n\n<h3 id=\"spoken-language\">Spoken language</h3>\n\n<p>The national curriculum for mathematics reflects the importance of spoken language in pupils’ development across the whole curriculum – cognitively, socially and linguistically. The quality and variety of language that pupils hear and speak are key factors in developing their mathematical vocabulary and presenting a mathematical justification, argument or proof. They must be assisted in making their thinking clear to themselves as well as others, and teachers should ensure that pupils build secure foundations by using discussion to probe and remedy their misconceptions.</p>\n\n<h3 id=\"school-curriculum\">School curriculum</h3>\n\n<p>The programmes of study for mathematics are set out year-by-year for key stages 1 and 2. Schools are, however, only required to teach the relevant programme of study by the end of the key stage. Within each key stage, schools therefore have the flexibility to introduce content earlier or later than set out in the programme of study. In addition, schools can introduce key stage content during an earlier key stage, if appropriate. All schools are also required to set out their school curriculum for mathematics on a year-by-year basis and make this information available online.</p>\n\n<h3 id=\"attainment-targets\">Attainment targets</h3>\n\n<p>By the end of each key stage, pupils are expected to know, apply and understand the matters, skills and processes specified in the relevant programme of study.</p>\n\n<div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<p>Schools are not required by law to teach the example content in [square brackets] or the content indicated as being ‘non-statutory’.</p>\n</div>\n\n<h2 id=\"key-stage-1---years-1-and-2\">Key stage 1 - years 1 and 2</h2>\n\n<p>The principal focus of mathematics teaching in key stage 1 is to ensure that pupils develop confidence and mental fluency with whole numbers, counting and place value. This should involve working with numerals, words and the 4 operations, including with practical resources [for example, concrete objects and measuring tools].</p>\n\n<p>At this stage, pupils should develop their ability to recognise, describe, draw, compare and sort different shapes and use the related vocabulary. Teaching should also involve using a range of measures to describe and compare different quantities such as length, mass, capacity/volume, time and money.</p>\n\n<p>By the end of year 2, pupils should know the number bonds to 20 and be precise in using and understanding place value. An emphasis on practice at this early stage will aid fluency.</p>\n\n<p>Pupils should read and spell mathematical vocabulary, at a level consistent with their increasing word reading and spelling knowledge at key stage 1.</p>\n\n<h2 id=\"year-1-programme-of-study\">Year 1 programme of study</h2>\n\n<h3 id=\"number---number-and-place-value\">Number - number and place value</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>count to and across 100, forwards and backwards, beginning with 0 or 1, or from any given number</li>\n  <li>count, read and write numbers to 100 in numerals; count in multiples of 2s, 5s and 10s</li>\n  <li>given a number, identify 1 more and 1 less</li>\n  <li>identify and represent numbers using objects and pictorial representations including the number line, and use the language of: equal to, more than, less than (fewer), most, least</li>\n  <li>read and write numbers from 1 to 20 in numerals and words</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n\n<p>Pupils practise counting (1, 2, 3…), ordering (for example, first, second, third…), and to indicate a quantity (for example, 3 apples, 2 centimetres), including solving simple concrete problems, until they are fluent.<br><br>\nPupils begin to recognise place value in numbers beyond 20 by reading, writing, counting and comparing numbers up to 100, supported by objects and pictorial representations.<br><br>\nThey practise counting as reciting numbers and counting as enumerating objects, and counting in 2s, 5s and 10s from different multiples to develop their recognition of patterns in the number system (for example, odd and even numbers), including varied and frequent practice through increasingly complex questions.<br><br>\nThey recognise and create repeating patterns with objects and with shapes.</p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"number---addition-and-subtraction\">Number - addition and subtraction</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>read, write and interpret mathematical statements involving addition (+), subtraction (−) and equals (=) signs</li>\n  <li>represent and use number bonds and related subtraction facts within 20</li>\n  <li>add and subtract one-digit and two-digit numbers to 20, including 0</li>\n  <li>solve one-step problems that involve addition and subtraction, using concrete objects and pictorial representations, and missing number problems such as 7 = ? − 9</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n\n<p>Pupils memorise and reason with number bonds to 10 and 20 in several forms (for example, 9 + 7 = 16; 16 − 7 = 9; 7 = 16 − 9). They should realise the effect of adding or subtracting 0. This establishes addition and subtraction as related operations.<br><br>\nPupils combine and increase numbers, counting forwards and backwards.<br><br>\nThey discuss and solve problems in familiar practical contexts, including using quantities. Problems should include the terms: put together, add, altogether, total, take away, distance between, difference between, more than and less than, so that pupils develop the concept of addition and subtraction and are enabled to use these operations flexibly.</p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"number---multiplication-and-division\">Number - multiplication and division</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>solve one-step problems involving multiplication and division, by calculating the answer using concrete objects, pictorial representations and arrays with the support of the teacher</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n\n<p>Through grouping and sharing small quantities, pupils begin to understand: multiplication and division; doubling numbers and quantities; and finding simple fractions of objects, numbers and quantities.<br><br>\nThey make connections between arrays, number patterns, and counting in 2s, 5s and 10s.</p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"number---fractions\">Number - fractions</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>recognise, find and name a half as 1 of 2 equal parts of an object, shape or quantity</li>\n  <li>recognise, find and name a quarter as 1 of 4 equal parts of an object, shape or quantity</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n\n<p>Pupils are taught half and quarter as ‘fractions of’ discrete and continuous quantities by solving problems using shapes, objects and quantities. For example, they could recognise and find half a length, quantity, set of objects or shape. Pupils connect halves and quarters to the equal sharing and grouping of sets of objects and to measures, as well as recognising and combining halves and quarters as parts of a whole.</p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"measurement\">Measurement</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>compare, describe and solve practical problems for: \n    <ul>\n<li>lengths and heights [for example, long/short, longer/shorter, tall/short, double/half]</li>\n      <li>mass/weight [for example, heavy/light, heavier than, lighter than]</li>\n      <li>capacity and volume [for example, full/empty, more than, less than, half, half full, quarter]</li>\n      <li>time [for example, quicker, slower, earlier, later]</li>\n    </ul>\n</li>\n  <li>measure and begin to record the following:\n    <ul>\n<li>lengths and heights</li>\n      <li>mass/weight</li>\n      <li>capacity and volume</li>\n      <li>time (hours, minutes, seconds)</li>\n      <li>recognise and know the value of different denominations of coins and notes</li>\n      <li>sequence events in chronological order using language [for example, before and after, next, first, today, yesterday, tomorrow, morning, afternoon and evening]</li>\n    </ul>\n</li>\n  <li>recognise and use language relating to dates, including days of the week, weeks, months and years</li>\n  <li>tell the time to the hour and half past the hour and draw the hands on a clock face to show these times</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n\n<p>The pairs of terms: mass and weight, volume and capacity, are used interchangeably at this stage.<br><br>\nPupils move from using and comparing different types of quantities and measures using non-standard units, including discrete (for example, counting) and continuous (for example, liquid) measurement, to using manageable common standard units.<br><br>\nIn order to become familiar with standard measures, pupils begin to use measuring tools such as a ruler, weighing scales and containers.<br><br>\nPupils use the language of time, including telling the time throughout the day, first using o’clock and then half past.</p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"geometry---properties-of-shapes\">Geometry - properties of shapes</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>recognise and name common 2-D and 3-D shapes, including:\n    <ul>\n<li>2-D shapes [for example, rectangles (including squares), circles and triangles]</li>\n      <li>3-D shapes [for example, cuboids (including cubes), pyramids and spheres]</li>\n    </ul>\n</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n\n<p>Pupils handle common 2-D and 3-D shapes, naming these and related everyday objects fluently. They recognise these shapes in different orientations and sizes, and know that rectangles, triangles, cuboids and pyramids are not always similar to each other.<br><br></p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"geometry---position-and-direction\">Geometry - position and direction</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>describe position, direction and movement, including whole, half, quarter and three-quarter turns</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n\n<p>Pupils use the language of position, direction and motion, including: left and right, top, middle and bottom, on top of, in front of, above, between, around, near, close and far, up and down, forwards and backwards, inside and outside.<br><br>\nPupils make whole, half, quarter and three-quarter turns in both directions and connect turning clockwise with movement on a clock face.</p>\n</div>\n\n<h2 id=\"year-2-programme-of-study\">Year 2 programme of study</h2>\n\n<h3 id=\"number---number-and-place-value-1\">Number - number and place value</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>count in steps of 2, 3, and 5 from 0, and in 10s from any number, forward and backward</li>\n  <li>recognise the place value of each digit in a two-digit number (10s, 1s)</li>\n  <li>identify, represent and estimate numbers using different representations, including the number line </li>\n  <li>compare and order numbers from 0 up to 100; use &lt;, &gt; and = signs</li>\n  <li>read and write numbers to at least 100 in numerals and in words</li>\n  <li>use place value and number facts to solve problems</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n\n<p>Using materials and a range of representations, pupils practise counting, reading, writing and comparing numbers to at least 100 and solving a variety of related problems to develop fluency. They count in multiples of 3 to support their later understanding of a third.<br><br>\nAs they become more confident with numbers up to 100, pupils are introduced to larger numbers to develop further their recognition of patterns within the number system and represent them in different ways, including spatial representations.<br><br>\nPupils should partition numbers in different ways (for example, 23 = 20 + 3 and 23 = 10 + 13) to support subtraction. They become fluent and apply their knowledge of numbers to reason with, discuss and solve problems that emphasise the value of each digit in two-digit numbers. They begin to understand 0 as a place holder.</p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"number---addition-and-subtraction-1\">Number - addition and subtraction</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>solve problems with addition and subtraction: \n    <ul>\n<li>using concrete objects and pictorial representations, including those involving numbers, quantities and measures</li>\n      <li>applying their increasing knowledge of mental and written methods </li>\n    </ul>\n</li>\n  <li>recall and use addition and subtraction facts to 20 fluently, and derive and use related facts up to 100</li>\n  <li>add and subtract numbers using concrete objects, pictorial representations, and mentally, including:\n    <ul>\n<li>a two-digit number and 1s</li>\n      <li>a two-digit number and 10s</li>\n      <li>2 two-digit numbers</li>\n      <li>adding 3 one-digit numbers</li>\n    </ul>\n</li>\n  <li>show that addition of 2 numbers can be done in any order (commutative) and subtraction of 1 number from another cannot </li>\n  <li>recognise and use the inverse relationship between addition and subtraction and use this to check calculations and solve missing number problems</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n\n<p>Pupils extend their understanding of the language of addition and subtraction to include sum and difference.<br><br>\nPupils practise addition and subtraction to 20 to become increasingly fluent in deriving facts such as using 3 + 7 = 10; 10 − 7 = 3 and 7 = 10 − 3 to calculate 30 + 70 = 100; 100 − 70 = 30 and 70 = 100 − 30. They check their calculations, including by adding to check subtraction and adding numbers in a different order to check addition (for example, 5 + 2 + 1 = 1 + 5 + 2 = 1 + 2 + 5). This establishes commutativity and associativity of addition.<br><br>\nRecording addition and subtraction in columns supports place value and prepares for formal written methods with larger numbers.</p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"number---multiplication-and-division-1\">Number - multiplication and division</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>recall and use multiplication and division facts for the 2, 5 and 10 multiplication tables, including recognising odd and even numbers</li>\n  <li>calculate mathematical statements for multiplication and division within the multiplication tables and write them using the multiplication (×), division (÷) and equals (=) signs</li>\n  <li>show that multiplication of 2 numbers can be done in any order (commutative) and division of 1 number by another cannot </li>\n  <li>solve problems involving multiplication and division, using materials, arrays, repeated addition, mental methods, and multiplication and division facts, including problems in contexts</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n<p>Pupils use a variety of language to describe multiplication and division.<br><br>\nPupils are introduced to the multiplication tables. They practise to become fluent in the 2, 5 and 10 multiplication tables and connect them to each other. They connect the 10 multiplication table to place value, and the 5 multiplication table to the divisions on the clock face. They begin to use other multiplication tables and recall multiplication facts, including using related division facts to perform written and mental calculations.<br><br>\nPupils work with a range of materials and contexts in which multiplication and division relate to grouping and sharing discrete and continuous quantities, to arrays and to repeated addition. They begin to relate these to fractions and measures (for example, 40 ÷ 2 = 20, 20 is a half of 40). They use commutativity and inverse relations to develop multiplicative reasoning (for example, 4 × 5 = 20 and 20 ÷ 5 = 4).</p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"number---fractions-1\">Number - fractions</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>recognise, find, name and write fractions <span class=\"fraction\">\n  <img alt=\"1/3\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/1_3-9003d7f3d7cd4433647a5f6525aa7eda.png\"></span>\n, <span class=\"fraction\">\n  <img alt=\"1/4\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/1_4-b6128849c8da3b46b9cb5a6918cfe084.png\"></span>\n, <span class=\"fraction\">\n  <img alt=\"2/4\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/2_4-e071530a44f0d7980f3442c23e3edd3b.png\"></span>\n and <span class=\"fraction\">\n  <img alt=\"3/4\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/3_4-cded12d0389211f864dcb27e640c64d4.png\"></span>\n of a length, shape, set of objects or quantity</li>\n  <li>write simple fractions, for example <span class=\"fraction\">\n  <img alt=\"1/2\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/1_2-6e6f542bec97cb8ea3acf39cd25690ee.png\"></span>\n of 6 = 3 and recognise the equivalence of <span class=\"fraction\">\n  <img alt=\"2/4\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/2_4-e071530a44f0d7980f3442c23e3edd3b.png\"></span>\nand <span class=\"fraction\">\n  <img alt=\"1/2\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/1_2-6e6f542bec97cb8ea3acf39cd25690ee.png\"></span>\n</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n\n<p>Pupils use fractions as ‘fractions of’ discrete and continuous quantities by solving problems using shapes, objects and quantities. They connect unit fractions to equal sharing and grouping, to numbers when they can be calculated, and to measures, finding fractions of lengths, quantities, sets of objects or shapes. They meet <span class=\"fraction\">\n    <img alt=\"3/4\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/3_4-cded12d0389211f864dcb27e640c64d4.png\"></span>\n as the first example of a non-unit fraction.<br><br>\nPupils should count in fractions up to 10, starting from any number and using the <span class=\"fraction\">\n    <img alt=\"1/2\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/1_2-6e6f542bec97cb8ea3acf39cd25690ee.png\"></span>\n and <span class=\"fraction\">\n    <img alt=\"2/4\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/2_4-e071530a44f0d7980f3442c23e3edd3b.png\"></span>\n  equivalence on the number line (for example, 1<span class=\"fraction\">\n    <img alt=\"1/4\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/1_4-b6128849c8da3b46b9cb5a6918cfe084.png\"></span>\n, 1<span class=\"fraction\">\n    <img alt=\"2/4\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/2_4-e071530a44f0d7980f3442c23e3edd3b.png\"></span>\n (or 1<span class=\"fraction\">\n    <img alt=\"1/2\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/1_2-6e6f542bec97cb8ea3acf39cd25690ee.png\"></span>\n), 1<span class=\"fraction\">\n    <img alt=\"3/4\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/3_4-cded12d0389211f864dcb27e640c64d4.png\"></span>\n, 2). This reinforces the concept of fractions as numbers and that they can add up to more than 1.</p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"measurement-1\">Measurement</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>choose and use appropriate standard units to estimate and measure length/height in any direction (m/cm); mass (kg/g); temperature (°C); capacity (litres/ml) to the nearest appropriate unit, using rulers, scales, thermometers and measuring vessels</li>\n  <li>compare and order lengths, mass, volume/capacity and record the results using &gt;, &lt; and =</li>\n  <li>recognise and use symbols for pounds (£) and pence (p); combine amounts to make a particular value </li>\n  <li>find different combinations of coins that equal the same amounts of money</li>\n  <li>solve simple problems in a practical context involving addition and subtraction of money of the same unit, including giving change </li>\n  <li>compare and sequence intervals of time</li>\n  <li>tell and write the time to five minutes, including quarter past/to the hour and draw the hands on a clock face to show these times</li>\n  <li>know the number of minutes in an hour and the number of hours in a day</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n\n<p>Pupils use standard units of measurement with increasing accuracy, using their knowledge of the number system. They use the appropriate language and record using standard abbreviations.<br><br>\nComparing measures includes simple multiples such as ‘half as high’; ‘twice as wide’.<br><br>\nPupils become fluent in telling the time on analogue clocks and recording it.<br><br>\nThey become fluent in counting and recognising coins. They read and say amounts of money confidently and use the symbols £ and p accurately, recording pounds and pence separately.</p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"geometry---properties-of-shapes-1\">Geometry - properties of shapes</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>identify and describe the properties of 2-D shapes, including the number of sides, and line symmetry in a vertical line</li>\n  <li>identify and describe the properties of 3-D shapes, including the number of edges, vertices and faces</li>\n  <li>identify 2-D shapes on the surface of 3-D shapes, [for example, a circle on a cylinder and a triangle on a pyramid]</li>\n  <li>compare and sort common 2-D and 3-D shapes and everyday objects</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n\n<p>Pupils handle and name a wide variety of common 2-D and 3-D shapes including: quadrilaterals and polygons and cuboids, prisms and cones, and identify the properties of each shape (for example, number of sides, number of faces). Pupils identify, compare and sort shapes on the basis of their properties and use vocabulary precisely, such as sides, edges, vertices and faces.<br><br>\nPupils read and write names for shapes that are appropriate for their word reading and spelling.<br><br>\nPupils draw lines and shapes using a straight edge.</p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"geometry---position-and-direction-1\">Geometry - position and direction</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>order and arrange combinations of mathematical objects in patterns and sequences</li>\n  <li>use mathematical vocabulary to describe position, direction and movement, including movement in a straight line and distinguishing between rotation as a turn and in terms of right angles for quarter, half and three-quarter turns (clockwise and anti-clockwise)</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n<p>Pupils should work with patterns of shapes, including those in different orientations.<br><br>\nPupils use the concept and language of angles to describe ‘turn’ by applying rotations, including in practical contexts (for example, pupils themselves moving in turns, giving instructions to other pupils to do so, and programming robots using instructions given in right angles).</p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"statistics\">Statistics</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>interpret and construct simple pictograms, tally charts, block diagrams and tables</li>\n  <li>ask and answer simple questions by counting the number of objects in each category and sorting the categories by quantity</li>\n  <li>ask-and-answer questions about totalling and comparing categorical data</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n<p>Pupils record, interpret, collate, organise and compare information (for example, using many-to-one correspondence in pictograms with simple ratios 2, 5,10).</p>\n</div>\n\n<h2 id=\"lower-key-stage-2---years-3-and-4\">Lower key stage 2 - years 3 and 4</h2>\n\n<p>The principal focus of mathematics teaching in lower key stage 2 is to ensure that pupils become increasingly fluent with whole numbers and the 4 operations, including number facts and the concept of place value. This should ensure that pupils develop efficient written and mental methods and perform calculations accurately with increasingly large whole numbers.</p>\n\n<p>At this stage, pupils should develop their ability to solve a range of problems, including with simple fractions and decimal place value. Teaching should also ensure that pupils draw with increasing accuracy and develop mathematical reasoning so they can analyse shapes and their properties, and confidently describe the relationships between them. It should ensure that they can use measuring instruments with accuracy and make connections between measure and number.</p>\n\n<p>By the end of year 4, pupils should have memorised their multiplication tables up to and including the 12 multiplication table and show precision and fluency in their work.</p>\n\n<p>Pupils should read and spell mathematical vocabulary correctly and confidently, using their growing word-reading knowledge and their knowledge of spelling.</p>\n\n<h2 id=\"year-3-programme-of-study\">Year 3 programme of study</h2>\n\n<h3 id=\"number---number-and-place-value-2\">Number - number and place value</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>count from 0 in multiples of 4, 8, 50 and 100; find 10 or 100 more or less than a given number</li>\n  <li>recognise the place value of each digit in a 3-digit number (100s, 10s, 1s)</li>\n  <li>compare and order numbers up to 1,000</li>\n  <li>identify, represent and estimate numbers using different representations</li>\n  <li>read and write numbers up to 1,000 in numerals and in words</li>\n  <li>solve number problems and practical problems involving these ideas</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n<p>Pupils now use multiples of 2, 3, 4, 5, 8, 10, 50 and 100.<br><br>\nThey use larger numbers to at least 1,000, applying partitioning related to place value using varied and increasingly complex problems, building on work in year 2 (for example, 146 = 100 + 40 + 6, 146 = 130 +16).<br><br>\nUsing a variety of representations, including those related to measure, pupils continue to count in 1s, 10s and 100s, so that they become fluent in the order and place value of numbers to 1,000.</p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"number---addition-and-subtraction-2\">Number - addition and subtraction</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>add and subtract numbers mentally, including: \n    <ul>\n<li>a three-digit number and 1s</li>\n      <li>a three-digit number and 10s</li>\n      <li>a three-digit number and 100s</li>\n    </ul>\n</li>\n  <li>add and subtract numbers with up to 3 digits, using formal written methods of columnar addition and subtraction </li>\n  <li>estimate the answer to a calculation and use inverse operations to check answers </li>\n  <li>solve problems, including missing number problems, using number facts, place value, and more complex addition and subtraction</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n<p>Pupils practise solving varied addition and subtraction questions. For mental calculations with two-digit numbers, the answers could exceed 100.<br><br>\nPupils use their understanding of place value and partitioning, and practise using columnar addition and subtraction with increasingly large numbers up to 3 digits to become fluent (see <a href=\"/government/uploads/system/uploads/attachment_data/file/238967/Mathematics_Appendix_1.pdf\">Mathematics Appendix 1</a>).</p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"number---multiplication-and-division-2\">Number - multiplication and division</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>recall and use multiplication and division facts for the 3, 4 and 8 multiplication tables</li>\n  <li>write and calculate mathematical statements for multiplication and division using the multiplication tables that they know, including for two-digit numbers times one-digit numbers, using mental and progressing to formal written methods </li>\n  <li>solve problems, including missing number problems, involving multiplication and division, including positive integer scaling problems and correspondence problems in which n objects are connected to m objects</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n\n<p>Pupils continue to practise their mental recall of multiplication tables when they are calculating mathematical statements in order to improve fluency. Through doubling, they connect the 2, 4 and 8 multiplication tables.<br><br>\nPupils develop efficient mental methods, for example, using commutativity and associativity (for example, 4 × 12 × 5 = 4 × 5 × 12 = 20 × 12 = 240) and multiplication and division facts (for example, using 3 × 2 = 6, 6 ÷ 3 = 2 and 2 = 6 ÷ 3) to derive related facts (30 × 2 = 60, 60 ÷ 3 = 20 and 20 = 60 ÷ 3).<br><br>\nPupils develop reliable written methods for multiplication and division, starting with calculations of two-digit numbers by one-digit numbers and progressing to the formal written methods of short multiplication and division.<br><br>\nPupils solve simple problems in contexts, deciding which of the 4 operations to use and why. These include measuring and scaling contexts, (for example 4 times as high, 8 times as long etc) and correspondence problems in which m objects are connected to n objects (for example, 3 hats and 4 coats, how many different outfits?; 12 sweets shared equally between 4 children; 4 cakes shared equally between 8 children).</p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"number---fractions-2\">Number - fractions</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>count up and down in tenths; recognise that tenths arise from dividing an object into 10 equal parts and in dividing one-digit numbers or quantities by 10</li>\n  <li>recognise, find and write fractions of a discrete set of objects: unit fractions and non-unit fractions with small denominators</li>\n  <li>recognise and use fractions as numbers: unit fractions and non-unit fractions with small denominators</li>\n  <li>recognise and show, using diagrams, equivalent fractions with small denominators</li>\n  <li>add and subtract fractions with the same denominator within one whole [for example, <span class=\"fraction\">\n  <img alt=\"5/7\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/5_7-49f56ee6fd62ced2d259627c2b76f289.png\"></span>\n+<span class=\"fraction\">\n  <img alt=\"1/7\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/1_7-6a115beb7006b4845828335625bcf483.png\"></span>\n = <span class=\"fraction\">\n  <img alt=\"6/7\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/6_7-058de36653bd10a0c23f9d992e3186f6.png\"></span>\n]</li>\n  <li>compare and order unit fractions, and fractions with the same denominators</li>\n  <li>solve problems that involve all of the above</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n\n<p>Pupils connect tenths to place value, decimal measures and to division by 10.<br><br>\nThey begin to understand unit and non-unit fractions as numbers on the number line, and deduce relations between them, such as size and equivalence. They should go beyond the [0, 1] interval, including relating this to measure.<br><br>\nPupils understand the relation between unit fractions as operators (fractions of), and division by integers.<br><br>\nThey continue to recognise fractions in the context of parts of a whole, numbers, measurements, a shape, and unit fractions as a division of a quantity.<br><br>\nPupils practise adding and subtracting fractions with the same denominator through a variety of increasingly complex problems to improve fluency.</p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"measurement-2\">Measurement</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>measure, compare, add and subtract: lengths (m/cm/mm); mass (kg/g); volume/capacity (l/ml) </li>\n  <li>measure the perimeter of simple 2-D shapes</li>\n  <li>add and subtract amounts of money to give change, using both £ and p in practical contexts</li>\n  <li>tell and write the time from an analogue clock, including using Roman numerals from I to XII, and 12-hour and 24-hour clocks</li>\n  <li>estimate and read time with increasing accuracy to the nearest minute; record and compare time in terms of seconds, minutes and hours; use vocabulary such as o’clock, am/pm, morning, afternoon, noon and midnight</li>\n  <li>know the number of seconds in a minute and the number of days in each month, year and leap year</li>\n  <li>compare durations of events [for example, to calculate the time taken by particular events or tasks]</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n\n<p>Pupils continue to measure using the appropriate tools and units, progressing to using a wider range of measures, including comparing and using mixed units (for example, 1 kg and 200g) and simple equivalents of mixed units (for example, 5m = 500cm).<br><br>\nThe comparison of measures includes simple scaling by integers (for example, a given quantity or measure is twice as long or 5 times as high) and this connects to multiplication.<br><br>\nPupils continue to become fluent in recognising the value of coins, by adding and subtracting amounts, including mixed units, and giving change using manageable amounts. They record £ and p separately. The decimal recording of money is introduced formally in year 4.<br><br>\nPupils use both analogue and digital 12-hour clocks and record their times. In this way they become fluent in and prepared for using digital 24-hour clocks in year 4.</p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"geometry---properties-of-shapes-2\">Geometry - properties of shapes</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>draw 2-D shapes and make 3-D shapes using modelling materials; recognise 3-D shapes in different orientations and describe them</li>\n  <li>recognise angles as a property of shape or a description of a turn</li>\n  <li>identify right angles, recognise that 2 right angles make a half-turn, 3 make three-quarters of a turn and 4 a complete turn; identify whether angles are greater than or less than a right angle </li>\n  <li>identify horizontal and vertical lines and pairs of perpendicular and parallel lines</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n\n<p>Pupils’ knowledge of the properties of shapes is extended at this stage to symmetrical and non-symmetrical polygons and polyhedra. Pupils extend their use of the properties of shapes. They should be able to describe the properties of 2-D and 3-D shapes using accurate language, including lengths of lines and acute and obtuse for angles greater or lesser than a right angle.<br><br>\nPupils connect decimals and rounding to drawing and measuring straight lines in centimetres, in a variety of contexts.</p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"statistics-1\">Statistics</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>interpret and present data using bar charts, pictograms and tables </li>\n  <li>solve one-step and two-step questions [for example ‘How many more?’ and ‘How many fewer?’] using information presented in scaled bar charts and pictograms and tables</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n\n<p>Pupils understand and use simple scales (for example, 2, 5, 10 units per cm) in pictograms and bar charts with increasing accuracy.<br><br>\nThey continue to interpret data presented in many contexts.</p>\n</div>\n\n<h2 id=\"year-4-programme-of-study\">Year 4 programme of study</h2>\n\n<h3 id=\"number---number-and-place-value-3\">Number - number and place value</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>count in multiples of 6, 7, 9, 25 and 1,000</li>\n  <li>find 1,000 more or less than a given number</li>\n  <li>count backwards through 0 to include negative numbers</li>\n  <li>recognise the place value of each digit in a four-digit number (1,000s, 100s, 10s, and 1s) </li>\n  <li>order and compare numbers beyond 1,000</li>\n  <li>identify, represent and estimate numbers using different representations </li>\n  <li>round any number to the nearest 10, 100 or 1,000 </li>\n  <li>solve number and practical problems that involve all of the above and with increasingly large positive numbers</li>\n  <li>read Roman numerals to 100 (I to C) and know that over time, the numeral system changed to include the concept of 0 and place value</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n<p>Using a variety of representations, including measures, pupils become fluent in the order and place value of numbers beyond 1,000, including counting in 10s and 100s, and maintaining fluency in other multiples through varied and frequent practice.<br><br>\nThey begin to extend their knowledge of the number system to include the decimal numbers and fractions that they have met so far.<br><br>\nThey connect estimation and rounding numbers to the use of measuring instruments.<br><br>\nRoman numerals should be put in their historical context so pupils understand that there have been different ways to write whole numbers and that the important concepts of 0 and place value were introduced over a period of time.</p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"number---addition-and-subtraction-3\">Number - addition and subtraction</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>add and subtract numbers with up to 4 digits using the formal written methods of columnar addition and subtraction where appropriate </li>\n  <li>estimate and use inverse operations to check answers to a calculation</li>\n  <li>solve addition and subtraction two-step problems in contexts, deciding which operations and methods to use and why</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n\n<p>Pupils continue to practise both mental methods and columnar addition and subtraction with increasingly large numbers to aid fluency (see <a href=\"/government/uploads/system/uploads/attachment_data/file/238967/Mathematics_Appendix_1.pdf\">Mathematics Appendix 1</a>).</p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"number---multiplication-and-division-3\">Number - multiplication and division</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>recall multiplication and division facts for multiplication tables up to 12 × 12</li>\n  <li>use place value, known and derived facts to multiply and divide mentally, including: multiplying by 0 and 1; dividing by 1; multiplying together 3 numbers</li>\n  <li>recognise and use factor pairs and commutativity in mental calculations</li>\n  <li>multiply two-digit and three-digit numbers by a one-digit number using formal written layout</li>\n  <li>solve problems involving multiplying and adding, including using the distributive law to multiply two-digit numbers by 1 digit, integer scaling problems and harder correspondence problems such as n objects are connected to m objects</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n\n<p>Pupils continue to practise recalling and using multiplication tables and related division facts to aid fluency.<br><br>\nPupils practise mental methods and extend this to 3-digit numbers to derive facts, (for example 600 ÷ 3 = 200 can be derived from 2 x 3 = 6).<br><br>\nPupils practise to become fluent in the formal written method of short multiplication and short division with exact answers (see <a href=\"/government/uploads/system/uploads/attachment_data/file/238967/Mathematics_Appendix_1.pdf\">Mathematics Appendix 1</a>).<br><br>\nPupils write statements about the equality of expressions (for example, use the distributive law 39 × 7 = 30 × 7 + 9 × 7 and associative law (2 × 3) × 4 = 2 × (3 × 4)). They combine their knowledge of number facts and rules of arithmetic to solve mental and written calculations for example, 2 x 6 x 5 = 10 x 6 = 60.<br><br>\nPupils solve two-step problems in contexts, choosing the appropriate operation, working with increasingly harder numbers. This should include correspondence questions such as the numbers of choices of a meal on a menu, or 3 cakes shared equally between 10 children.</p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"number---fractions-including-decimals\">Number - fractions (including decimals)</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>recognise and show, using diagrams, families of common equivalent fractions </li>\n  <li>count up and down in hundredths; recognise that hundredths arise when dividing an object by 100 and dividing tenths by 10</li>\n  <li>solve problems involving increasingly harder fractions to calculate quantities, and fractions to divide quantities, including non-unit fractions where the answer is a whole number</li>\n  <li>add and subtract fractions with the same denominator</li>\n  <li>recognise and write decimal equivalents of any number of tenths or hundreds</li>\n  <li>\n    <p>recognise and write decimal equivalents to <span class=\"fraction\">\n  <img alt=\"1/4\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/1_4-b6128849c8da3b46b9cb5a6918cfe084.png\"></span>\n, <span class=\"fraction\">\n  <img alt=\"1/2\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/1_2-6e6f542bec97cb8ea3acf39cd25690ee.png\"></span>\n, <span class=\"fraction\">\n  <img alt=\"3/4\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/3_4-cded12d0389211f864dcb27e640c64d4.png\"></span></p>\n  </li>\n  <li>find the effect of dividing a one- or two-digit number by 10 and 100, identifying the value of the digits in the answer as ones, tenths and hundredths </li>\n  <li>round decimals with 1 decimal place to the nearest whole number</li>\n  <li>compare numbers with the same number of decimal places up to 2 decimal places</li>\n  <li>solve simple measure and money problems involving fractions and decimals to 2 decimal places</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n\n<p>Pupils should connect hundredths to tenths and place value and decimal measure.<br><br>\nThey extend the use of the number line to connect fractions, numbers and measures.<br><br>\nPupils understand the relation between non-unit fractions and multiplication and division of quantities, with particular emphasis on tenths and hundredths.<br><br>\nPupils make connections between fractions of a length, of a shape and as a representation of one whole or set of quantities. Pupils use factors and multiples to recognise equivalent fractions and simplify where appropriate (for example, <span class=\"fraction\">\n    <img alt=\"6/9\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/6_9-ba0a8863e047e14d8b55a5c9faf5e9ab.png\"></span>\n = <span class=\"fraction\">\n    <img alt=\"2/3\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/2_3-435b14b4b37e978ea0e50f971bf3a0ed.png\"></span>\n or <span class=\"fraction\">\n    <img alt=\"1/4\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/1_4-b6128849c8da3b46b9cb5a6918cfe084.png\"></span>\n = <span class=\"fraction\">\n    <img alt=\"2/8\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/2_8-cf40b8c85c1793c26e73b92a5975b635.png\"></span>\n).<br><br>\nPupils continue to practise adding and subtracting fractions with the same denominator, to become fluent through a variety of increasingly complex problems beyond one whole. \nPupils are taught throughout that decimals and fractions are different ways of expressing numbers and proportions. <br><br>\nPupils’ understanding of the number system and decimal place value is extended at this stage to tenths and then hundredths. This includes relating the decimal notation to division of whole number by 10 and later 100.<br><br>\nThey practise counting using simple fractions and decimals, both forwards and backwards.<br><br>\nPupils learn decimal notation and the language associated with it, including in the context of measurements. They make comparisons and order decimal amounts and quantities that are expressed to the same number of decimal places.
```
