They should be able to represent numbers with 1 or 2 decimal places in several ways, such as on number lines.</p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"measurement-3\">Measurement</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>convert between different units of measure [for example, kilometre to metre; hour to minute]</li>\n  <li>measure and calculate the perimeter of a rectilinear figure (including squares) in centimetres and metres</li>\n  <li>find the area of rectilinear shapes by counting squares</li>\n  <li>estimate, compare and calculate different measures, including money in pounds and pence </li>\n  <li>read, write and convert time between analogue and digital 12- and 24-hour clocks</li>\n  <li>solve problems involving converting from hours to minutes, minutes to seconds, years to months, weeks to days</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n<p>Pupils build on their understanding of place value and decimal notation to record metric measures, including money.<br><br>\nThey use multiplication to convert from larger to smaller units.<br><br>\nPerimeter can be expressed algebraically as 2(a + b) where a and b are the dimensions in the same unit.<br><br>\nThey relate area to arrays and multiplication.</p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"geometry---properties-of-shapes-3\">Geometry - properties of shapes</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>compare and classify geometric shapes, including quadrilaterals and triangles, based on their properties and sizes</li>\n  <li>identify acute and obtuse angles and compare and order angles up to 2 right angles by size</li>\n  <li>identify lines of symmetry in 2-D shapes presented in different orientations</li>\n  <li>complete a simple symmetric figure with respect to a specific line of symmetry</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n\n<p>Pupils continue to classify shapes using geometrical properties, extending to classifying different triangles (for example, isosceles, equilateral, scalene) and quadrilaterals (for example, parallelogram, rhombus, trapezium).<br><br>\nPupils compare and order angles in preparation for using a protractor and compare lengths and angles to decide if a polygon is regular or irregular.<br><br>\nPupils draw symmetric patterns using a variety of media to become familiar with different orientations of lines of symmetry; and recognise line symmetry in a variety of diagrams, including where the line of symmetry does not dissect the original shape.</p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"geometry---position-and-direction-2\">Geometry - position and direction</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>describe positions on a 2-D grid as coordinates in the first quadrant</li>\n  <li>describe movements between positions as translations of a given unit to the left/right and up/down</li>\n  <li>plot specified points and draw sides to complete a given polygon</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n<p>Pupils draw a pair of axes in one quadrant, with equal scales and integer labels. They read, write and use pairs of co-ordinates, for example (2, 5), including using co-ordinate-plotting ICT tools.</p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"statistics-2\">Statistics</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>interpret and present discrete and continuous data using appropriate graphical methods, including bar charts and time graphs</li>\n  <li>solve comparison, sum and difference problems using information presented in bar charts, pictograms, tables and other graphs</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n\n<p>Pupils understand and use a greater range of scales in their representations.<br><br>\nPupils begin to relate the graphical representation of data to recording change over time.</p>\n</div>\n\n<h2 id=\"upper-key-stage-2---years-5-and-6\">Upper key stage 2 - years 5 and 6</h2>\n\n<p>The principal focus of mathematics teaching in upper key stage 2 is to ensure that pupils extend their understanding of the number system and place value to include larger integers. This should develop the connections that pupils make between multiplication and division with fractions, decimals, percentages and ratio.</p>\n\n<p>At this stage, pupils should develop their ability to solve a wider range of problems, including increasingly complex properties of numbers and arithmetic, and problems demanding efficient written and mental methods of calculation. With this foundation in arithmetic, pupils are introduced to the language of algebra as a means for solving a variety of problems. Teaching in geometry and measures should consolidate and extend knowledge developed in number. Teaching should also ensure that pupils classify shapes with increasingly complex geometric properties and that they learn the vocabulary they need to describe them.</p>\n\n<p>By the end of year 6, pupils should be fluent in written methods for all 4 operations, including long multiplication and division, and in working with fractions, decimals and percentages.</p>\n\n<p>Pupils should read, spell and pronounce mathematical vocabulary correctly. </p>\n\n<h2 id=\"year-5-programme-of-study\">Year 5 programme of study</h2>\n\n<h3 id=\"number---number-and-place-value-4\">Number - number and place value</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>read, write, order and compare numbers to at least 1,000,000 and determine the value of each digit</li>\n  <li>count forwards or backwards in steps of powers of 10 for any given number up to 1,000,000</li>\n  <li>interpret negative numbers in context, count forwards and backwards with positive and negative whole numbers, including through 0</li>\n  <li>round any number up to 1,000,000 to the nearest 10, 100, 1,000, 10,000 and 100,000</li>\n  <li>solve number problems and practical problems that involve all of the above</li>\n  <li>read Roman numerals to 1,000 (M) and recognise years written in Roman numerals</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n\n<p>Pupils identify the place value in large whole numbers.<br><br>\nThey continue to use number in context, including measurement. Pupils extend and apply their understanding of the number system to the decimal numbers and fractions that they have met so far.<br><br>\nThey should recognise and describe linear number sequences (for example, 3, 3<span class=\"fraction\">\n    <img alt=\"1/2\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/1_2-6e6f542bec97cb8ea3acf39cd25690ee.png\"></span>\n, 4, 4<span class=\"fraction\">\n    <img alt=\"1/2\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/1_2-6e6f542bec97cb8ea3acf39cd25690ee.png\"></span>\n …), including those involving fractions and decimals, and find the term-to-term rule in words (for example, add <span class=\"fraction\">\n    <img alt=\"1/2\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/1_2-6e6f542bec97cb8ea3acf39cd25690ee.png\"></span>\n).</p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"number---addition-and-subtraction-4\">Number - addition and subtraction</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>add and subtract whole numbers with more than 4 digits, including using formal written methods (columnar addition and subtraction)</li>\n  <li>add and subtract numbers mentally with increasingly large numbers</li>\n  <li>use rounding to check answers to calculations and determine, in the context of a problem, levels of accuracy</li>\n  <li>solve addition and subtraction multi-step problems in contexts, deciding which operations and methods to use and why</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n\n<p>Pupils practise using the formal written methods of columnar addition and subtraction with increasingly large numbers to aid fluency (see <a href=\"/government/uploads/system/uploads/attachment_data/file/238967/Mathematics_Appendix_1.pdf\">Mathematics Appendix 1</a>).<br><br>\nThey practise mental calculations with increasingly large numbers to aid fluency (for example, 12,462 – 2,300 = 10,162).</p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"number---multiplication-and-division-4\">Number - multiplication and division</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>identify multiples and factors, including finding all factor pairs of a number, and common factors of 2 numbers </li>\n  <li>know and use the vocabulary of prime numbers, prime factors and composite (non-prime) numbers</li>\n  <li>establish whether a number up to 100 is prime and recall prime numbers up to 19</li>\n  <li>multiply numbers up to 4 digits by a one- or two-digit number using a formal written method, including long multiplication for two-digit numbers</li>\n  <li>multiply and divide numbers mentally, drawing upon known facts</li>\n  <li>divide numbers up to 4 digits by a one-digit number using the formal written method of short division and interpret remainders appropriately for the context </li>\n  <li>multiply and divide whole numbers and those involving decimals by 10, 100 and 1,000</li>\n  <li>recognise and use square numbers and cube numbers, and the notation for squared (²) and cubed (³)</li>\n  <li>solve problems involving multiplication and division, including using their knowledge of factors and multiples, squares and cubes</li>\n  <li>solve problems involving addition, subtraction, multiplication and division and a combination of these, including understanding the meaning of the equals sign</li>\n  <li>solve problems involving multiplication and division, including scaling by simple fractions and problems involving simple rates</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n\n<p>Pupils practise and extend their use of the formal written methods of short multiplication and short division (see <a href=\"/government/uploads/system/uploads/attachment_data/file/238967/Mathematics_Appendix_1.pdf\">Mathematics Appendix 1</a>). They apply all the multiplication tables and related division facts frequently, commit them to memory and use them confidently to make larger calculations.<br><br>\nThey use and understand the terms factor, multiple and prime, square and cube numbers.<br><br>\nPupils interpret non-integer answers to division by expressing results in different ways according to the context, including with remainders, as fractions, as decimals or by rounding (for example, 98 ÷ 4 = <span class=\"fraction\">\n    <img alt=\"98/4\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/98_4-9ba334750e0b2baa5de23f7f403edeab.png\"></span>\n = 24 r 2 = 24<span class=\"fraction\">\n    <img alt=\"1/2\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/1_2-6e6f542bec97cb8ea3acf39cd25690ee.png\"></span>\n = 24.5 ≈ 25).<br><br>\nPupils use multiplication and division as inverses to support the introduction of ratio in year 6, for example, by multiplying and dividing by powers of 10 in scale drawings or by multiplying and dividing by powers of a 1,000 in converting between units such as kilometres and metres.<br><br>\nDistributivity can be expressed as a(b + c) = ab + ac.<br><br>\nThey understand the terms factor, multiple and prime, square and cube numbers and use them to construct equivalence statements (for example, 4 x 35 = 2 x 2 x 35; 3 x 270  = 3 x 3 x 9 x 10 = 9² x 10).<br><br>\nPupils use and explain the equals sign to indicate equivalence, including in missing number problems (for example 13 + 24 = 12 + 25; 33 = 5 x ?).</p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"number---fractions-including-decimals-and-percentages\">Number - fractions (including decimals and percentages)</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>compare and order fractions whose denominators are all multiples of the same number</li>\n  <li>identify, name and write equivalent fractions of a given fraction, represented visually, including tenths and hundredths </li>\n  <li>recognise mixed numbers and improper fractions and convert from one form to the other and write mathematical statements &gt; 1 as a mixed number [for example, <span class=\"fraction\">\n  <img alt=\"2/5\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/2_5-5a3f90368c7e257ece44695d16ef8d84.png\"></span>\n+<span class=\"fraction\">\n  <img alt=\"4/5\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/4_5-4cd2b9091787311659b43ab293809463.png\"></span>\n = <span class=\"fraction\">\n  <img alt=\"6/5\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/6_5-4e95057840acb7e1d4854d583d44a302.png\"></span>\n= 1 <span class=\"fraction\">\n  <img alt=\"1/5\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/1_5-a0f3cba7fd9f5e72b4221648ea38b59e.png\"></span>\n ] </li>\n  <li>add and subtract fractions with the same denominator, and denominators that are multiples of the same number</li>\n  <li>multiply proper fractions and mixed numbers by whole numbers, supported by materials and diagrams</li>\n  <li>read and write decimal numbers as fractions [for example, 0.71 = <span class=\"fraction\">\n  <img alt=\"71/100\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/71_100-e5ecc7e495709bddca067de679bc0421.png\"></span>\n ] </li>\n  <li>recognise and use thousandths and relate them to tenths, hundredths and decimal equivalents</li>\n  <li>round decimals with 2 decimal places to the nearest whole number and to 1 decimal place</li>\n  <li>read, write, order and compare numbers with up to 3 decimal places</li>\n  <li>solve problems involving number up to 3 decimal places </li>\n  <li>recognise the per cent symbol (%) and understand that per cent relates to ‘number of parts per 100’, and write percentages as a fraction with denominator 100, and as a decimal fraction</li>\n  <li>solve problems which require knowing percentage and decimal equivalents of <span class=\"fraction\">\n  <img alt=\"1/2\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/1_2-6e6f542bec97cb8ea3acf39cd25690ee.png\"></span>\n, <span class=\"fraction\">\n  <img alt=\"1/4\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/1_4-b6128849c8da3b46b9cb5a6918cfe084.png\"></span>\n, <span class=\"fraction\">\n  <img alt=\"1/5\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/1_5-a0f3cba7fd9f5e72b4221648ea38b59e.png\"></span>\n, <span class=\"fraction\">\n  <img alt=\"2/5\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/2_5-5a3f90368c7e257ece44695d16ef8d84.png\"></span>\n, <span class=\"fraction\">\n  <img alt=\"4/5\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/4_5-4cd2b9091787311659b43ab293809463.png\"></span>\n and those fractions with a denominator of a multiple of 10 or 25</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught throughout that percentages, decimals and fractions are different ways of expressing proportions.<br><br>\nThey extend their knowledge of fractions to thousandths and connect to decimals and measures.<br><br>\nPupils connect equivalent fractions &gt; 1 that simplify to integers with division and other fractions &gt; 1 to division with remainders, using the number line and other models, and hence move from these to improper and mixed fractions.<br><br>\nPupils connect multiplication by a fraction to using fractions as operators (fractions of), and to division, building on work from previous years. This relates to scaling by simple fractions, including fractions &gt; 1.<br><br>\nPupils practise adding and subtracting fractions to become fluent through a variety of increasingly complex problems. They extend their understanding of adding and subtracting fractions to calculations that exceed 1 as a mixed number.<br><br>\nPupils continue to practise counting forwards and backwards in simple fractions.<br><br>\nPupils continue to develop their understanding of fractions as numbers, measures and operators by finding fractions of numbers and quantities.\nPupils extend counting from year 4, using decimals and fractions including bridging 0, for example on a number line.<br><br>\nPupils say, read and write decimal fractions and related tenths, hundredths and thousandths accurately and are confident in checking the reasonableness of their answers to problems.<br><br>\nThey mentally add and subtract tenths, and one-digit whole numbers and tenths.<br><br>\nThey practise adding and subtracting decimals, including a mix of whole numbers and decimals, decimals with different numbers of decimal places, and complements of 1 (for example, 0.83 + 0.17 = 1).<br><br>\nPupils should go beyond the measurement and money models of decimals, for example, by solving puzzles involving decimals.<br><br>\nPupils should make connections between percentages, fractions and decimals (for example, 100% represents a whole quantity and 1% is <span class=\"fraction\">\n    <img alt=\"1/100\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/1_100-692ce06fee1e5fd86e4f69361e28dfbe.png\"></span>\n, 50% is <span class=\"fraction\">\n    <img alt=\"50/100\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/50_100-0d702d5b2f8417e016042255e9057dbc.png\"></span>\n, 25% is <span class=\"fraction\">\n    <img alt=\"25/100\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/25_100-25ef46453c2b60492e5112d433109dd5.png\"></span>\n) and relate this to finding ‘fractions of’.</p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"measurement-4\">Measurement</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>convert between different units of metric measure [for example, kilometre and metre; centimetre and metre; centimetre and millimetre; gram and kilogram; litre and millilitre]</li>\n  <li>understand and use approximate equivalences between metric units and common imperial units such as inches, pounds and pints </li>\n  <li>measure and calculate the perimeter of composite rectilinear shapes in centimetres and metres</li>\n  <li>calculate and compare the area of rectangles (including squares), including using standard units, square centimetres (cm²) and square metres (m²), and estimate the area of irregular shapes </li>\n  <li>estimate volume [for example, using 1 cm³ blocks to build cuboids (including cubes)] and capacity [for example, using water]</li>\n  <li>solve problems involving converting between units of time </li>\n  <li>use all four operations to solve problems involving measure [for example, length, mass, volume, money] using decimal notation, including scaling</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n\n<p>Pupils use their knowledge of place value and multiplication and division to convert between standard units.<br><br>\nPupils calculate the perimeter of rectangles and related composite shapes, including using the relations of perimeter or area to find unknown lengths. Missing measures questions such as these can be expressed algebraically, for example 4 + 2b = 20 for a rectangle of sides 2 cm and b cm and perimeter of 20cm.<br><br>\nPupils calculate the area from scale drawings using given measurements.<br><br>\nPupils use all 4 operations in problems involving time and money, including conversions (for example, days to weeks, expressing the answer as weeks and days).</p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"geometry---properties-of-shapes-4\">Geometry - properties of shapes</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>identify 3-D shapes, including cubes and other cuboids, from 2-D representations</li>\n  <li>know angles are measured in degrees: estimate and compare acute, obtuse and reflex angles</li>\n  <li>draw given angles, and measure them in degrees (°)</li>\n  <li>identify:\n    <ul>\n<li>angles at a point and 1 whole turn (total 360°)</li>\n      <li>angles at a point on a straight line and half a turn (total 180°)</li>\n      <li>other multiples of 90°</li>\n      <li>use the properties of rectangles to deduce related facts and find missing lengths and angles </li>\n      <li>distinguish between regular and irregular polygons based on reasoning about equal sides and angles</li>\n    </ul>\n</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n\n<p>Pupils become accurate in drawing lines with a ruler to the nearest millimetre, and measuring with a protractor. They use conventional markings for parallel lines and right angles.<br><br>\nPupils use the term diagonal and make conjectures about the angles formed between sides, and between diagonals and parallel sides, and other properties of quadrilaterals, for example using dynamic geometry ICT tools.<br><br>\nPupils use angle sum facts and other properties to make deductions about missing angles and relate these to missing number problems.</p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"geometry---position-and-direction-3\">Geometry - position and direction</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>identify, describe and represent the position of a shape following a reflection or translation, using the appropriate language, and know that the shape has not changed</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n\n<p>Pupils recognise and use reflection and translation in a variety of diagrams, including continuing to use a 2-D grid and coordinates in the first quadrant. Reflection should be in lines that are parallel to the axes.</p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"statistics-3\">Statistics</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>solve comparison, sum and difference problems using information presented in a line graph</li>\n  <li>complete, read and interpret information in tables, including timetables</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n<p>Pupils connect their work on coordinates and scales to their interpretation of time graphs.<br><br>\nThey begin to decide which representations of data are most appropriate and why.</p>\n</div>\n\n<h2 id=\"year-6-programme-of-study\">Year 6 programme of study</h2>\n\n<h3 id=\"number---number-and-place-value-5\">Number - number and place value</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>read, write, order and compare numbers up to 10,000,000 and determine the value of each digit</li>\n  <li>round any whole number to a required degree of accuracy</li>\n  <li>use negative numbers in context, and calculate intervals across 0</li>\n  <li>solve number and practical problems that involve all of the above</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n\n<p>Pupils use the whole number system, including saying, reading and writing numbers accurately.</p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"number----addition-subtraction-multiplication-and-division\">Number -  addition, subtraction, multiplication and division</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>multiply multi-digit numbers up to 4 digits by a two-digit whole number using the formal written method of long multiplication </li>\n  <li>divide numbers up to 4 digits by a two-digit whole number using the formal written method of long division, and interpret remainders as whole number remainders, fractions, or by rounding, as appropriate for the context</li>\n  <li>divide numbers up to 4 digits by a two-digit number using the formal written method of short division where appropriate, interpreting remainders according to the context </li>\n  <li>perform mental calculations, including with mixed operations and large numbers</li>\n  <li>identify common factors, common multiples and prime numbers</li>\n  <li>use their knowledge of the order of operations to carry out calculations involving the 4 operations</li>\n  <li>solve addition and subtraction multi-step problems in contexts, deciding which operations and methods to use and why</li>\n  <li>solve problems involving addition, subtraction, multiplication and division</li>\n  <li>use estimation to check answers to calculations and determine, in the context of a problem, an appropriate degree of accuracy</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n\n<p>Pupils practise addition, subtraction, multiplication and division for larger numbers, using the formal written methods of columnar addition and subtraction, short and long multiplication, and short and long division (see <a href=\"/government/uploads/system/uploads/attachment_data/file/238967/Mathematics_Appendix_1.pdf\">Mathematics Appendix 1</a>).<br><br>\nThey undertake mental calculations with increasingly large numbers and more complex calculations.<br><br>\nPupils continue to use all the multiplication tables to calculate mathematical statements in order to maintain their fluency.<br><br>\nPupils round answers to a specified degree of accuracy, for example, to the nearest 10, 20, 50, etc, but not to a specified number of significant figures.<br><br>\nPupils explore the order of operations using brackets; for example, 2 + 1 x 3 = 5 and (2 + 1) x 3 = 9.<br><br>\nCommon factors can be related to finding equivalent fractions.</p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"number---fractions-including-decimals-and-percentages-1\">Number - Fractions (including decimals and percentages)</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>use common factors to simplify fractions; use common multiples to express fractions in the same denomination</li>\n  <li>compare and order fractions, including fractions &gt;1</li>\n  <li>add and subtract fractions with different denominators and mixed numbers, using the concept of equivalent fractions</li>\n  <li>multiply simple pairs of proper fractions, writing the answer in its simplest form [for example, <span class=\"fraction\">\n  <img alt=\"1/4\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/1_4-b6128849c8da3b46b9cb5a6918cfe084.png\"></span>\n × <span class=\"fraction\">\n  <img alt=\"1/2\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/1_2-6e6f542bec97cb8ea3acf39cd25690ee.png\"></span>\n = <span class=\"fraction\">\n  <img alt=\"1/8\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/1_8-ab835c5e48c8e96817a98c10f014e08a.png\"></span>\n]</li>\n  <li>divide proper fractions by whole numbers [for example, <span class=\"fraction\">\n  <img alt=\"1/3\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/1_3-9003d7f3d7cd4433647a5f6525aa7eda.png\"></span>\n ÷ 2 = <span class=\"fraction\">\n  <img alt=\"1/6\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/1_6-2b902096fc0d403b9f07e2b682b4c2a8.png\"></span>\n]</li>\n  <li>associate a fraction with division and calculate decimal fraction equivalents [for example, 0.375] for a simple fraction [for example, <span class=\"fraction\">\n  <img alt=\"3/8\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/3_8-a19899b009e630d4edbde75a01919e2b.png\"></span>\n]</li>\n  <li>identify the value of each digit in numbers given to 3 decimal places and multiply and divide numbers by 10, 100 and 1,000 giving answers up to 3 decimal places</li>\n  <li>multiply one-digit numbers with up to 2 decimal places by whole numbers</li>\n  <li>use written division methods in cases where the answer has up to 2 decimal places </li>\n  <li>solve problems which require answers to be rounded to specified degrees of accuracy</li>\n  <li>recall and use equivalences between simple fractions, decimals and percentages, including in different contexts</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n\n<p>Pupils should practise, use and understand the addition and subtraction of fractions with different denominators by identifying equivalent fractions with the same denominator. They should start with fractions where the denominator of one fraction is a multiple of the other (for example, <span class=\"fraction\">\n    <img alt=\"1/2\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/1_2-6e6f542bec97cb8ea3acf39cd25690ee.png\"></span>\n+<span class=\"fraction\">\n    <img alt=\"1/8\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/1_8-ab835c5e48c8e96817a98c10f014e08a.png\"></span>\n = <span class=\"fraction\">\n    <img alt=\"5/8\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/5_8-742aabe0df816c6619b3cdfb897e8605.png\"></span>\n] and progress to varied and increasingly complex problems.<br><br>\nPupils should use a variety of images to support their understanding of multiplication with fractions. This follows earlier work about fractions as operators (fractions of), as numbers, and as equal parts of objects, for example as parts of a rectangle.<br><br>\nPupils use their understanding of the relationship between unit fractions and division to work backwards by multiplying a quantity that represents a unit fraction to find the whole quantity (for example, if quarter of a length is 36cm, then the whole length is 36 × 4 = 144cm).<br><br>\nThey practise calculations with simple fractions and decimal fraction equivalents to aid fluency, including listing equivalent fractions to identify fractions with common denominators.<br><br>\nPupils can explore and make conjectures about converting a simple fraction to a decimal fraction (for example, 3 ÷ 8 = 0.375). For simple fractions with recurring decimal equivalents, pupils learn about rounding the decimal to three decimal places, or other appropriate approximations depending on the context. Pupils multiply and divide numbers with up to two decimal places by one-digit and two-digit whole numbers. Pupils multiply decimals by whole numbers, starting with the simplest cases, such as 0.4 × 2 = 0.8, and in practical contexts, such as measures and money.<br><br>\nPupils are introduced to the division of decimal numbers by one-digit whole numbers, initially, in practical contexts involving measures and money. They recognise division calculations as the inverse of multiplication.<br><br>\nPupils also develop their skills of rounding and estimating as a means of predicting and checking the order of magnitude of their answers to decimal calculations. This includes rounding answers to a specified degree of accuracy and checking the reasonableness of their answers.</p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"ratio-and-proportion\">Ratio and proportion</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>solve problems involving the relative sizes of 2 quantities where missing values can be found by using integer multiplication and division facts</li>\n  <li>solve problems involving the calculation of percentages [for example, of measures and such as 15% of 360] and the use of percentages for comparison</li>\n  <li>solve problems involving similar shapes where the scale factor is known or can be found</li>\n  <li>solve problems involving unequal sharing and grouping using knowledge of fractions and multiples</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n\n<p>Pupils recognise proportionality in contexts when the relations between quantities are in the same ratio (for example, similar shapes and recipes).<br><br>\nPupils link percentages or 360° to calculating angles of pie charts.<br><br>\nPupils should consolidate their understanding of ratio when comparing quantities, sizes and scale drawings by solving a variety of problems. They might use the notation a:b to record their work.<br><br>\nPupils solve problems involving unequal quantities, for example, ’for every egg you need 3 spoonfuls of flour’, ‘<span class=\"fraction\">\n    <img alt=\"3/5\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/3_5-7790e5633ca2a7af9906e7819cb4212e.png\"></span>\n  of the class are boys’. These problems are the foundation for later formal approaches to ratio and proportion.</p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"algebra\">Algebra</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>use simple formulae</li>\n  <li>generate and describe linear number sequences</li>\n  <li>express missing number problems algebraically</li>\n  <li>find pairs of numbers that satisfy an equation with 2 unknowns</li>\n  <li>enumerate possibilities of combinations of 2 variables</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n<p>Pupils should be introduced to the use of symbols and letters to represent variables and unknowns in mathematical situations that they already understand, such as: </p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>missing numbers, lengths, coordinates and angles</li>\n  <li>formulae in mathematics and science</li>\n  <li>equivalent expressions (for example, a + b = b + a)</li>\n  <li>generalisations of number patterns</li>\n  <li>number puzzles (for example, what 2 numbers can add up to)</li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"measurement-5\">Measurement</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>solve problems involving the calculation and conversion of units of measure, using decimal notation up to 3 decimal places where appropriate</li>\n  <li>use, read, write and convert between standard units, converting measurements of length, mass, volume and time from a smaller unit of measure to a larger unit, and vice versa, using decimal notation to up to 3 decimal places</li>\n  <li>convert between miles and kilometres</li>\n  <li>recognise that shapes with the same areas can have different perimeters and vice versa</li>\n  <li>recognise when it is possible to use formulae for area and volume of shapes </li>\n  <li>calculate the area of parallelograms and triangles</li>\n  <li>calculate, estimate and compare volume of cubes and cuboids using standard units, including cubic centimetres (cm³) and cubic metres (m³), and extending to other units [for example, mm³ and km³]</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n\n<p>Pupils connect conversion (for example, from kilometres to miles) to a graphical representation as preparation for understanding linear/proportional graphs.<br><br>\nThey know approximate conversions and are able to tell if an answer is sensible.<br><br>\nUsing the number line, pupils use, add and subtract positive and negative integers for measures such as temperature.<br><br>\nThey relate the area of rectangles to parallelograms and triangles, for example, by dissection, and calculate their areas, understanding and using the formulae (in words or symbols) to do this.<br><br>\nPupils could be introduced to compound units for speed, such as miles per hour, and apply their knowledge in science or other subjects as appropriate.</p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"geometry---properties-of-shapes-5\">Geometry - properties of shapes</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>draw 2-D shapes using given dimensions and angles </li>\n  <li>recognise, describe and build simple 3-D shapes, including making nets</li>\n  <li>compare and classify geometric shapes based on their properties and sizes and find unknown angles in any triangles, quadrilaterals, and regular polygons</li>\n  <li>illustrate and name parts of circles, including radius, diameter and circumference and know that the diameter is twice the radius </li>\n  <li>recognise angles where they meet at a point, are on a straight line, or are vertically opposite, and find missing angles</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n\n<p>Pupils draw shapes and nets accurately, using measuring tools and conventional markings and labels for lines and angles.<br><br>\nPupils describe the properties of shapes and explain how unknown angles and lengths can be derived from known measurements.<br><br>\nThese relationships might be expressed algebraically for example, d = 2 × r; a = 180 − (b + c).</p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"geometry---position-and-direction-4\">Geometry - position and direction</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>describe positions on the full coordinate grid (all 4 quadrants) </li>\n  <li>draw and translate simple shapes on the coordinate plane, and reflect them in the axes</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n\n<p>Pupils draw and label a pair of axes in all 4 quadrants with equal scaling. This extends their knowledge of one quadrant to all 4 quadrants, including the use of negative numbers.<br><br>\nPupils draw and label rectangles (including squares), parallelograms and rhombuses, specified by coordinates in the four quadrants, predicting missing coordinates using the properties of shapes. These might be expressed algebraically for example, translating vertex (a, b) to (a − 2, b + 3); (a, b) and (a + d, b + d) being opposite vertices of a square of side d.</p>\n</div>\n\n<h3 id=\"statistics-4\">Statistics</h3>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>interpret and construct pie charts and line graphs and use these to solve problems</li>\n  <li>calculate and interpret the mean as an average</li>\n</ul><div class=\"call-to-action\">\n<h4>Notes and guidance (non-statutory)<br><br>\n</h4>\n\n<p>Pupils connect their work on angles, fractions and percentages to the interpretation of pie charts.<br><br>\nPupils both encounter and draw graphs relating 2 variables, arising from their own enquiry and in other subjects.<br><br>\nThey should connect conversion from kilometres to miles in measurement to its graphical representation.<br><br>\nPupils know when it is appropriate to find the mean of a data set.</p>\n</div>\n\n<h2 id=\"key-stage-3\">Key stage 3</h2>\n\n<h3 id=\"introduction\">Introduction</h3>\n\n<p>Mathematics is an interconnected subject in which pupils need to be able to move fluently between representations of mathematical ideas. The programme of study for key stage 3 is organised into apparently distinct domains, but pupils should build on key stage 2 and connections across mathematical ideas to develop fluency, mathematical reasoning and competence in solving increasingly sophisticated problems. They should also apply their mathematical knowledge in science, geography, computing and other subjects.</p>\n\n<p>Decisions about progression should be based on the security of pupils’ understanding and their readiness to progress to the next stage. Pupils who grasp concepts rapidly should be challenged through being offered rich and sophisticated problems before any acceleration through new content in preparation for key stage 4. Those who are not sufficiently fluent should consolidate their understanding, including through additional practice, before moving on. </p>\n\n<h3 id=\"working-mathematically\">Working mathematically</h3>\n\n<p>Through the mathematics content, pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<h4 id=\"develop-fluency\">Develop fluency</h4>\n\n<ul>\n<li>consolidate their numerical and mathematical capability from key stage 2 and extend their understanding of the number system and place value to include decimals, fractions, powers and roots</li>\n  <li>select and use appropriate calculation strategies to solve increasingly complex problems</li>\n  <li>use algebra to generalise the structure of arithmetic, including to formulate mathematical relationships</li>\n  <li>substitute values in expressions, rearrange and simplify expressions, and solve equations</li>\n  <li>move freely between different numerical, algebraic, graphical and diagrammatic representations [for example, equivalent fractions, fractions and decimals, and equations and graphs]</li>\n  <li>develop algebraic and graphical fluency, including understanding linear and simple quadratic functions</li>\n  <li>use language and properties precisely to analyse numbers, algebraic expressions, 2-D and 3-D shapes, probability and statistics</li>\n</ul><h4 id=\"reason-mathematically\">Reason mathematically</h4>\n\n<ul>\n<li>extend their understanding of the number system; make connections between number relationships, and their algebraic and graphical representations</li>\n  <li>extend and formalise their knowledge of ratio and proportion in working with measures and geometry, and in formulating proportional relations algebraically</li>\n  <li>identify variables and express relations between variables algebraically and graphically</li>\n  <li>make and test conjectures about patterns and relationships; look for proofs or counter-examples</li>\n  <li>begin to reason deductively in geometry, number and algebra, including using geometrical constructions</li>\n  <li>interpret when the structure of a numerical problem requires additive, multiplicative or proportional reasoning</li>\n  <li>explore what can and cannot be inferred in statistical and probabilistic settings, and begin to express their arguments formally</li>\n</ul><h4 id=\"solve-problems\">Solve problems</h4>\n\n<ul>\n<li>develop their mathematical knowledge, in part through solving problems and evaluating the outcomes, including multi-step problems</li>\n  <li>develop their use of formal mathematical knowledge to interpret and solve problems, including in financial mathematics</li>\n  <li>begin to model situations mathematically and express the results using a range of formal mathematical representations</li>\n  <li>select appropriate concepts, methods and techniques to apply to unfamiliar and non-routine problems</li>\n</ul><h3 id=\"subject-content\">Subject content</h3>\n\n<h4 id=\"number\">Number</h4>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to: </p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>understand and use place value for decimals, measures and integers of any size</li>\n  <li>order positive and negative integers, decimals and fractions; use the number line as a model for ordering of the real numbers; use the symbols =, ≠, &lt;, &gt;, ≤, ≥ </li>\n  <li>use the concepts and vocabulary of prime numbers, factors (or divisors), multiples, common factors, common multiples, highest common factor, lowest common multiple, prime factorisation, including using product notation and the unique factorisation property</li>\n  <li>use the 4 operations, including formal written methods, applied to integers, decimals, proper and improper fractions, and mixed numbers, all both positive and negative</li>\n  <li>use conventional notation for the priority of operations, including brackets, powers, roots and reciprocals</li>\n  <li>recognise and use relationships between operations including inverse operations</li>\n  <li>use integer powers and associated real roots (square, cube and higher), recognise powers of 2, 3, 4, 5  and distinguish between exact representations of roots and their decimal approximations </li>\n  <li>interpret and compare numbers in standard form A x 10<sup>n</sup> 1≤A&lt;10, where n is a positive or negative integer or 0</li>\n  <li>work interchangeably with terminating decimals and their corresponding fractions (such as 3.5 and <span class=\"fraction\">\n  <img alt=\"7/2\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/7_2-6c95273752b5a9800194bf0c5c32c673.png\"></span>\n or 0.375 and <span class=\"fraction\">\n  <img alt=\"3/8\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/3_8-a19899b009e630d4edbde75a01919e2b.png\"></span>\n)</li>\n  <li>define percentage as ‘number of parts per hundred’, interpret percentages and percentage changes as a fraction or a decimal, interpret these multiplicatively, express 1 quantity as a percentage of another, compare 2 quantities using percentages, and work with percentages greater than 100%</li>\n  <li>interpret fractions and percentages as operators</li>\n  <li>use standard units of mass, length, time, money and other measures, including with decimal quantities</li>\n  <li>round numbers and measures to an appropriate degree of accuracy [for example, to a number of decimal places or significant figures]</li>\n  <li>use approximation through rounding to estimate answers and calculate possible resulting errors expressed using inequality notation a&lt;x≤b</li>\n  <li>use a calculator and other technologies to calculate results accurately and then interpret them appropriately</li>\n  <li>appreciate the infinite nature of the sets of integers, real and rational numbers</li>\n</ul><h4 id=\"algebra-1\">Algebra</h4>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>use and interpret algebraic notation, including:\n    <ul>\n<li>ab in place of a × b</li>\n      <li>3y in place of y + y  + y and 3 × y</li>\n      <li>a² in place of a × a, a³ in place of a × a × a; a²b in place of a × a × b</li>\n      <li>\n<span class=\"fraction\">\n<img alt=\"a/b\" height=\"27\" src=\"https://assets.digital.cabinet-office.gov.uk/government/assets/fractions/a_b-0b8c38b38d9917b723f1809c2312f67b.png\"></span>\n in place of a ÷ b</li>\n      <li>coefficients written as fractions rather than as decimals</li>\n      <li>brackets</li>\n    </ul>\n</li>\n  <li>substitute numerical values into formulae and expressions, including scientific formulae</li>\n  <li>understand and use the concepts and vocabulary of expressions, equations, inequalities, terms and factors</li>\n  <li>simplify and manipulate algebraic expressions to maintain equivalence by:\n    <ul>\n<li>collecting like terms</li>\n      <li>multiplying a single term over a bracket</li>\n      <li>taking out common factors</li>\n      <li>expanding products of 2 or more binomials</li>\n    </ul>\n</li>\n  <li>understand and use standard mathematical formulae; rearrange formulae to change the subject</li>\n  <li>model situations or procedures by translating them into algebraic expressions or formulae and by using graphs</li>\n  <li>use algebraic methods to solve linear equations in 1 variable (including all forms that require rearrangement)</li>\n  <li>work with coordinates in all 4 quadrants</li>\n  <li>recognise, sketch and produce graphs of linear and quadratic functions of 1 variable with appropriate scaling, using equations in x and y and the Cartesian plane</li>\n  <li>interpret mathematical relationships both algebraically and graphically</li>\n  <li>reduce a given linear equation in two variables to the standard form y = mx + c; calculate and interpret gradients and intercepts of graphs of such linear equations numerically, graphically and algebraically</li>\n  <li>use linear and quadratic graphs to estimate values of y for given values of x and vice versa and to find approximate solutions of simultaneous linear equations</li>\n  <li>find approximate solutions to contextual problems from given graphs of a variety of functions, including piece-wise linear, exponential and reciprocal graphs</li>\n  <li>generate terms of a sequence from either a term-to-term or a position-to-term rule</li>\n  <li>recognise arithmetic sequences and find the nth term</li>\n  <li>recognise geometric sequences and appreciate other sequences that arise</li>\n</ul><h4 id=\"ratio-proportion-and-rates-of-change\">Ratio, proportion and rates of change</h4>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to: </p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>change freely between related standard units [for example time, length, area, volume/capacity, mass]</li>\n  <li>use scale factors, scale diagrams and maps</li>\n  <li>express 1 quantity as a fraction of another, where the fraction is less than 1 and greater than 1</li>\n  <li>use ratio notation, including reduction to simplest form</li>\n  <li>divide a given quantity into 2 parts in a given part:part or part:whole ratio; express the division of a quantity into 2 parts as a ratio</li>\n  <li>understand that a multiplicative relationship between 2 quantities can be expressed as a ratio or a fraction</li>\n  <li>relate the language of ratios and the associated calculations to the arithmetic of fractions and to linear functions</li>\n  <li>solve problems involving percentage change, including: percentage increase, decrease and original value problems and simple interest in financial mathematics</li>\n  <li>solve problems involving direct and inverse proportion, including graphical and algebraic representations</li>\n  <li>use compound units such as speed, unit pricing and density to solve problems</li>\n</ul><h4 id=\"geometry-and-measures\">Geometry and measures</h4>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to: </p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>derive and apply formulae to calculate and solve problems involving: perimeter and area of triangles, parallelograms, trapezia, volume of cuboids (including cubes) and other prisms (including cylinders)</li>\n  <li>calculate and solve problems involving: perimeters of 2-D shapes (including circles), areas of circles and composite shapes</li>\n  <li>draw and measure line segments and angles in geometric figures, including interpreting scale drawings</li>\n  <li>derive and use the standard ruler and compass constructions (perpendicular bisector of a line segment, constructing a perpendicular to a given line from/at a given point, bisecting a given angle); recognise and use the perpendicular distance from a point to a line as the shortest distance to the line </li>\n  <li>describe, sketch and draw using conventional terms and notations: points, lines, parallel lines, perpendicular lines, right angles, regular polygons, and other polygons that are reflectively and rotationally symmetric</li>\n  <li>use the standard conventions for labelling the sides and angles of triangle ABC, and know and use the criteria for congruence of triangles</li>\n  <li>derive and illustrate properties of triangles, quadrilaterals, circles, and other plane figures [for example, equal lengths and angles] using appropriate language and technologies</li>\n  <li>identify properties of, and describe the results of, translations, rotations and reflections applied to given figures</li>\n  <li>identify and construct congruent triangles, and construct similar shapes by enlargement, with and without coordinate grids</li>\n  <li>apply the properties of angles at a point, angles at a point on a straight line, vertically opposite angles</li>\n  <li>understand and use the relationship between parallel lines and alternate and corresponding angles</li>\n  <li>derive and use the sum of angles in a triangle and use it to deduce the angle sum in any polygon, and to derive properties of regular polygons</li>\n  <li>apply angle facts, triangle congruence, similarity and properties of quadrilaterals to derive results about angles and sides, including Pythagoras’ Theorem, and use known results to obtain simple proofs</li>\n  <li>use Pythagoras’ Theorem and trigonometric ratios in similar triangles to solve problems involving right-angled triangles</li>\n  <li>use the properties of faces, surfaces, edges and vertices of cubes, cuboids, prisms, cylinders, pyramids, cones and spheres to solve problems in 3-D</li>\n  <li>interpret mathematical relationships both algebraically and geometrically</li>\n</ul><h4 id=\"probability\">Probability</h4>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>record, describe and analyse the frequency of outcomes of simple probability experiments involving randomness, fairness, equally and unequally likely outcomes, using appropriate language and the 0-1 probability scale</li>\n  <li>understand that the probabilities of all possible outcomes sum to 1</li>\n  <li>enumerate sets and unions/intersections of sets systematically, using tables, grids and Venn diagrams</li>\n  <li>generate theoretical sample spaces for single and combined events with equally likely, mutually exclusive outcomes and use these to calculate theoretical probabilities </li>\n</ul><h4 id=\"statistics-5\">Statistics</h4>\n\n<p>Pupils should be taught to:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>describe, interpret and compare observed distributions of a single variable through: appropriate graphical representation involving discrete, continuous and grouped data; and appropriate measures of central tendency (mean, mode, median) and spread (range, consideration of outliers)</li>\n  <li>construct and interpret appropriate tables, charts, and diagrams, including frequency tables, bar charts, pie charts, and pictograms for categorical data, and vertical line (or bar) charts for ungrouped and grouped numerical data</li>\n  <li>describe simple mathematical relationships between 2 variables (bivariate data) in observational and experimental contexts and illustrate using scatter graphs</li>\n</ul><p>© Crown copyright 2013</p></div>",

  "content_id": "1d0ba5bd-8a0a-41a7-950a-c7b819da6336",
