a list price of over £40,000 when new pay a supplement of £310 per year on top of the standard rate, for five years.</p>\n\n<p>Creating a Roads Fund – From 2020-21 the government will spend all of the revenue raised from <abbr title=\"Vehicle Excise Duty\">VED</abbr> in England on the English Strategic Road Network.</p>\n\n<p>Air Passenger Duty (<abbr title=\"Air Passenger Duty\">APD</abbr>) devolution – The government is today publishing a discussion paper on options for supporting English regional airports with the impacts of <abbr title=\"Air Passenger Duty\">APD</abbr> devolution. </p>\n\n<p>Fuel duty for aqua-methanol – The government will legislate to apply a reduced rate of fuel duty to aqua-methanol in Finance Bill 2016. (Finance Bill 2016)</p>\n\n<p>Company car tax rates for 2019-20 – As announced at March Budget 2015, the appropriate percentage of list price subject to tax will increase by 3 percentage points for cars emitting more than 75 grams of carbon dioxide per kilometre (gCO2/km), to a maximum of 37%, in 2019-20. There will be a 3 percentage point differential between the 0-50 and 51-75 gCO2/km bands and between the 51-75 and 76-94 gCO2/km bands. (Finance Bill 2016) </p>\n\n<h5 id=\"environment-and-energy-taxes\">Environment and energy taxes</h5>\n\n<p>Climate Change Levy (<abbr title=\"Climate Change Levy\">CCL</abbr>) – The government will remove the Climate Change Levy exemption for renewably sourced electricity from 1 August 2015. There will be a transitional period for suppliers, from 1 August 2015, to claim the <abbr title=\"Climate Change Levy\">CCL</abbr> exemption on any renewable electricity that was generated before that date. The government will discuss the details of this transitional period with stakeholders over the summer and autumn, to determine an appropriate length for it. (Summer Finance Bill 2015, Finance Bill 2016) (23)</p>\n\n<p>Aggregates Levy – The government will reinstate exemptions from the Aggregates Levy that were recently found lawful by the European Commission. From 1 August, businesses can stop paying tax on the exempted materials and reclaim tax paid on these since the exemptions were suspended in April 2014. (Summer Finance Bill 2015) </p>\n\n<p>Environmental taxes – The government will continue to use the tax system to encourage positive environmental outcomes where tax is an effective instrument to do so, for example in reforming <abbr title=\"Vehicle Excise Duty\">VED</abbr> and the business energy tax landscape. The government will not extend the Coalition government’s commitment to increasing the proportion of revenue from environmental taxes to this Parliament, as such a target does not always reflect the success of government policy in achieving environmental outcomes. </p>\n\n<p>Business energy tax reform – The government will review the business energy efficiency tax landscape and consider approaches to simplify and improve the effectiveness of the regime. The review will consider the Climate Change Levy (<abbr title=\"Climate Change Levy\">CCL</abbr>), Carbon Reduction Commitment energy efficiency scheme and their interaction with other business energy efficiency policies and regulations. A consultation will be launched in the autumn. </p>\n\n<h5 id=\"property-tax\">Property tax</h5>\n\n<p>Stamp Duty Land Tax (<abbr title=\"Stamp Duty Land Tax\">SDLT</abbr>): application to certain authorised property funds As previously announced, the government intends to introduce a seeding relief for Property Authorised Investment Funds (PAIFs) and Co-ownership Authorised Contractual Schemes (CoACSs) and intends to make changes to the <abbr title=\"Stamp Duty Land Tax\">SDLT</abbr> treatment of CoACSs investing in property so that <abbr title=\"Stamp Duty Land Tax\">SDLT</abbr> does not arise on the transactions in units, subject to the resolution of potential avoidance issues. (Finance Bill 2016) </p>\n\n<p>Business rates: administration and avoidance – The government has today published progress updates on action it is taking to improve the administration of business rates, including the appeals system, and on tackling business rates avoidance. </p>\n\n<p>Business rates: local newspapers – The government is today publishing a consultation on the introduction of a business rates relief for local newspapers. </p>\n\n<h5 id=\"tax-simplification\">Tax simplification</h5>\n\n<p>Office of Tax Simplification (<abbr title=\"Office of Tax Simplification\">OTS</abbr>) – The government will establish the <abbr title=\"Office of Tax Simplification\">OTS</abbr> on a statutory basis as a permanent office of HM Treasury. Details will be published shortly. (Finance Bill 2016)</p>\n\n<p>Office of Tax Simplification report – The government will commission the <abbr title=\"Office of Tax Simplification\">OTS</abbr> to review the closer alignment of income tax and National Insurance contributions. </p>\n\n<p>Office of Tax Simplification report – The government will commission the <abbr title=\"Office of Tax Simplification\">OTS</abbr> to review the taxation of small companies. </p>\n\n<p>Consortium link company rule – As announced at Autumn Statement 2014, the government has, with effect from 10 December 2014, removed all requirements relating to the location of the ‘link company’ for consortium claims to group relief at section 133 Corporation Tax Act 2010 (<abbr title=\"Corporation Tax Act 2010\">CTA 2010</abbr>). This measure makes the tax system simpler by removing differences in treatment of link companies based in the UK and other jurisdictions. (Summer Finance Bill 2015) </p>\n\n<p>Taxation of employee benefits and expenses – As announced at Autumn Statement 2014, from April 2016 the government will simplify the tax system by introducing a statutory exemption for trivial benefits in kind costing less than £50. (Finance Bill 2016) </p>\n\n<p>Simplified expenses: legislative amendments – The government will amend the simplified expenses regime introduced in Finance Act 2013 to ensure that partnerships can fully access the provisions in respect of the use of a home and where business premises are also a home. (Finance Bill 2016) </p>\n\n<p>Self-employed National Insurance contributions – The government will consult in autumn 2015 on abolishing Class 2 National Insurance contributions (<abbr title=\"National Insurance contributions\">NICs</abbr>) and reforming Class 4 <abbr title=\"National Insurance contributions\">NICs</abbr> for the self-employed. </p>\n\n<p>Simplification of the treatment of termination payments – The government will consult on the tax and National Insurance contributions (<abbr title=\"National Insurance contributions\">NICs</abbr>) treatment of termination payments, to make the system simpler and fairer.</p>\n\n<p>Reviewing the rules for tax relief on travel and subsistence expense – As announced at Budget 2014, following a report by the <abbr title=\"Office of Tax Simplification\">OTS</abbr>, the government will review the rules underlying the tax treatment of travel and subsistence expenses. A discussion paper will be published shortly outlining a potential framework for new rules. </p>\n\n<p>Making tax easier – The government will publish a roadmap by the end of the year showing how it will transform tax administration for individuals and small businesses over this Parliament. Over the summer, <abbr title=\"HM Revenue and Customs\">HMRC</abbr> will begin discussing the policy choices underpinning this roadmap with key stakeholders and delivery partners, including small businesses and customer representatives. </p>\n\n<h5 id=\"hmrc-debtor-and-creditor-interest-rate\">\n<abbr title=\"HM Revenue and Customs\">HMRC</abbr> debtor and creditor interest rate</h5>\n\n<p>Simplification of <abbr title=\"HM Revenue and Customs\">HMRC</abbr> debtor and creditor interest rate – The government will set the rate of interest which applies on taxation-related debts payable under a court judgment or order by <abbr title=\"HM Revenue and Customs\">HMRC</abbr> to a rate equal to the Bank of England base rate plus 2%. The government will also apply the late payment interest rate of 3% to taxation-related debts owed to <abbr title=\"HM Revenue and Customs\">HMRC</abbr> under a court judgment or order. These changes will apply to new and pre-existing judgments and orders in respect of interest accruing on and after 8 July 2015. (Summer Finance Bill 2015)</p>\n\n<h4 id=\"tax-avoidance-and-tax-planning-evasion-and-compliance\">Tax avoidance and tax planning, evasion and compliance</h4>\n\n<h5 id=\"tax-evasion-fraud-and-compliance\">Tax evasion, fraud and compliance</h5>\n\n<p>Financial Intermediaries writing to their customers in advance of receipt of data under the Common Reporting Standard – The government will legislate to require financial intermediaries (including tax advisers) to notify their customers about the Common Reporting Standard, the penalties for evasion and the opportunities to disclose. (Summer Finance Bill 2015) </p>\n\n<p><abbr title=\"HM Revenue and Customs\">HMRC</abbr> tax enquiries: closure rules – At Autumn Statement 2014, the government announced a consultation on a proposal to introduce a new power, enabling <abbr title=\"HM Revenue and Customs\">HMRC</abbr> to achieve early resolution and closure of 1 or more aspects of a tax enquiry whilst leaving other aspects open. <abbr title=\"HM Revenue and Customs\">HMRC</abbr> will respond to this consultation during the summer. </p>\n\n<p>Direct recovery of debts – This government will introduce legislation to modernise and strengthen <abbr title=\"HM Revenue and Customs\">HMRC</abbr>’s powers to recover tax and tax credit debts directly from debtors’ bank and building society accounts, including funds held in cash ISAs. Having widely consulted, this measure will be subject to robust safeguards including a county court appeal process and a face-to-face visit to every debtor before they are considered for debt recovery through this measure. (Summer Finance Bill 2015) </p>\n\n<p>Criminal investigations – The government will increase funding to <abbr title=\"HM Revenue and Customs\">HMRC</abbr> by a total of over £60 million by 2020-21 to allow <abbr title=\"HM Revenue and Customs\">HMRC</abbr> to step up criminal investigations into serious and complex tax crime particularly focusing on wealthy individuals and corporates, with the aim of raising £600 million by the end of the Parliament. (33)</p>\n\n<p>Tackling the hidden economy – The government will extend <abbr title=\"HM Revenue and Customs\">HMRC</abbr>’s powers to acquire data from online intermediaries and electronic payment providers to find those operating in the hidden economy. We will legislate at Finance Bill 2016 to achieve this, following a consultation on the detail. We will invest in new <abbr title=\"HM Revenue and Customs\">HMRC</abbr> investigators from 2016 to exploit this data. The government will also create a digital disclosure channel which makes it simple for taxpayers to disclose unpaid tax liabilities. (Finance Bill 2016) (35)</p>\n\n<p>Additional compliance resource: local compliance – The government will invest around £300 million over 5 years from 2016 to tackle non-compliance by small and mid-sized businesses, public bodies and affluent individuals. This measure will result in additional tax receipts of over £2 billion by 2020-21. (36)</p>\n\n<h5 id=\"marketed-avoidance-schemes\">Marketed avoidance schemes</h5>\n\n<p>Serial avoiders – The government will publish a consultation, ahead of introducing legislation in Finance Bill 2016, for serial avoiders who persistently enter into tax avoidance schemes which are defeated. These include a special reporting requirement and a surcharge on those whose latest tax return is inaccurate as a result of a further defeated avoidance scheme, restricting access to reliefs for the minority who have a record of trying to abuse them, and developing further measures to name serial avoiders. The scope of the Promoters of Tax Avoidance Schemes regime would be widened by bringing in promoters whose schemes are regularly defeated. (Finance Bill 2016) </p>\n\n<p>General Anti-Abuse Rule (<abbr title=\"General Anti-Abuse Rule\">GAAR</abbr>) penalty – The government will publish a consultation to consider the detail of introducing a <abbr title=\"General Anti-Abuse Rule\">GAAR</abbr> penalty as well as considering new measures to strengthen the <abbr title=\"General Anti-Abuse Rule\">GAAR</abbr> further. (Finance Bill 2016) </p>\n\n<h5 id=\"business-tax\">Business tax</h5>\n\n<p>Large business tax compliance – The government will invest additional resources in large business compliance work to further extend our efforts to tackle evasion, avoidance and aggressive tax planning by large businesses. The government will also consult on new measures to increase compliance and tax transparency in relation to large business tax strategies. These will include the introduction of a ‘special measures’ regime to tackle businesses that persistently adopt highly aggressive behaviours including around tax planning, and a voluntary Code of Practice defining the standards <abbr title=\"HM Revenue and Customs\">HMRC</abbr> expects large businesses to meet in their relationship with <abbr title=\"HM Revenue and Customs\">HMRC</abbr>. (31)</p>\n\n<p>Controlled Foreign Companies (CFC) loss relief restriction – The government will remove the ability for companies to use UK losses and reliefs against a CFC charge from 8 July 2015. This will improve the effectiveness of the CFC regime in both deterring the diversion of profits and in taxing any profits that are diverted. (Summer Finance Bill 2015) (28)</p>\n\n<p>Disposal of stock other than in trade – The government will amend legislation relating to trading stock and intangible assets, to ensure that disposals made other than in the normal course of business are brought into account for tax purposes at full open market value. This amendment will stop corporate groups from using a transfer pricing override to manipulate the value of assets in intergroup transfers. (Summer Finance Bill 2015) (29)</p>\n\n<p>Taxation of carried interest: Base cost shifting and cherry picking – The government will introduce legislation, effective from 8 July 2015, to ensure that sums which arise to investment fund managers by way of carried interest will be charged to the full rate of capital gains tax, with only limited deductions being permitted. The government will also launch a consultation to better understand the activities of collective investment schemes, to determine under what circumstances performance returns should be taxed as a capital gain. It is not anticipated this will alter the tax treatment of carried interest. (Summer Finance Bill 2015) (27)</p>\n\n<h5 id=\"personal-tax\">Personal tax</h5>\n\n<p>Additional resource to target non-compliance by wealthy individuals – The government will provide additional resource to <abbr title=\"HM Revenue and Customs\">HMRC</abbr> to allow it to identify and tackle tax evasion and other non-compliance among wealthy individuals by extending <abbr title=\"HM Revenue and Customs\">HMRC</abbr>’s Customer Relationship Model to individuals with net wealth between £10-20 million, and to pursue more criminal investigations against wealthy individuals evading tax. The government will also consult on enhancing the information reported to <abbr title=\"HM Revenue and Customs\">HMRC</abbr> by wealthy individuals and trustees. (33)</p>\n\n<p>Additional specialist personal tax (SPT) resource – The government will invest an additional £36 million over 5 years from 2016 to tackle serious non-compliance by trusts, pension schemes and non-domiciled individuals. (32)</p>\n\n<p>Employment intermediaries and tax relief for travel and subsistence – As announced at March Budget 2015, the government has published a consultation document alongside the Summer Budget on detailed proposals to restrict tax relief for travel and subsistence for workers engaged through an employment intermediary, such as an umbrella company or a personal service company. The changes will take effect from 6 April 2016. (Finance Bill 2016)</p>\n\n<p>IR35 reform – The government will engage with stakeholders this year on how to improve the effectiveness of existing intermediaries legislation (‘IR35’) which is designed to protect against disguised employment. A discussion document will be published after Summer Budget 2015. </p>\n\n<h4 id=\"financial-services\">Financial services</h4>\n\n<p>Limited partnership consultation – The government will publish a consultation on technical changes to limited partnership legislation to enable private equity and venture capital investment funds to more effectively use the limited partnership structure. </p>\n\n<p>Office of Financial Sanctions Implementation – The government has reviewed the structures within HM Treasury for the implementation of financial sanctions and its work with the law enforcement community, to ensure these sanctions are properly enforced and businesses are made better aware of the rules they are being asked to comply with. The Chancellor of the Exchequer will establish this financial year an Office of Financial Sanctions Implementation within the Treasury. The Office will provide a high quality service to the private sector, working closely with law enforcement to help ensure that financial sanctions are properly understood, implemented and enforced. This will ensure financial sanctions make the fullest possible contributions to the UK’s foreign policy and national security goals and help maintain the integrity of and confidence in the UK financial services sector. The government will also legislate early in this Parliament to increase the penalties for non-compliance with financial sanctions. </p>\n\n<p>Competition in <abbr title=\"Small and medium-sized enterprise\">SME</abbr> lending – The government will introduce final legislation implementing 2 major reforms to the <abbr title=\"Small and medium-sized enterprise\">SME</abbr> lending market. The first will require the UK’s major banks to share credit information on their <abbr title=\"Small and medium-sized enterprise\">SME</abbr> customers with other finance providers through designated Credit Reference Agencies (CRAs). The second will require those same banks to offer SMEs they reject for finance the opportunity to be referred to a Finance Platform that can help match them with alternative lenders. </p>\n\n<h4 id=\"supply-side-reform-of-the-economy\">Supply side reform of the economy</h4>\n\n<h5 id=\"transport-and-infrastructure\">Transport and infrastructure</h5>\n\n<p>Roads Fund – The government will create a new Roads Fund, funded from 2020-21 directly by the revenues from vehicle excise duty to ensure continued high and stable investment in the strategic road network for generations to come.</p>\n\n<p>Roads Investment Strategy – The government will produce a second Roads Investment Strategy for the period 2020-25 before the end of this Parliament, based on this new Roads Fund.</p>\n\n<p>Rail fares – To help households with living costs, the government will continue to cap the increase in regulated rail fares to RPI for the whole of this Parliament.</p>\n\n<p>Network Rail: future shape and financing – The government has asked Nicola Shaw, Chief Executive of High Speed 1, to advise the government on how it should approach the longer-term future shape and financing of Network Rail. Nicola Shaw will work closely with Sir Peter Hendy, the new chairman of Network Rail, in conducting her work, which will be concluded before Budget 2016.</p>\n\n<p>Network Rail: devolving power to route managers – The government has asked Sir Peter Hendy and Mark Carne, Chief Executive of Network Rail, to continue with the work started in Network Rail to devolve more power to route managers closer to the front line, so that the railways are more focused on delivering what passengers need and to drive comparative benchmarking of the efficiency and effectiveness of individual routes – to drive up performance across the network.</p>\n\n<p>Network Rail: funding flows – The government will change the way it channels public money through the industry, directing it through the train operating companies, so that Network Rail focuses firmly on the needs of train operators and, through them, passengers. This will put the customers of the railway back in the driving seat in demanding efficiency and improvements that matter to them, making the best use of scarce capacity on the rail network.</p>\n\n<p>Network Rail: land and property – The government will establish a dedicated body to focus on pursuing opportunities to realise value from public land and property assets in the rail network to both maximise the benefit to local communities and reduce the burden of public debt.</p>\n\n<p>MOT – The government will explore the options for requiring motorists with new cars to undergo the first MOT after 4 years rather than 3, as part of the forthcoming Motoring Services Strategy. </p>\n\n<h5 id=\"energy-and-environment\">Energy and environment</h5>\n\n<p>Onshore electricity transmission – The government will publish proposals to extend competitive tendering to onshore electricity network transmission assets. </p>\n\n<p>Energy market switching – The government will work to increase switching in energy markets, as part of wider work to promote competition. In order to achieve this, government will:</p>\n\n<ul>\n  <li>\n    <p>work with Ofgem with the aim of introducing 24-hour switching by the end of 2018, building on previous action to reduce switching times to 17 days </p>\n  </li>\n  <li>\n    <p>work with industry to introduce a switching guarantee to improve trust in the switching process </p>\n  </li>\n  <li>\n    <p>further develop the use of Midata to facilitate effective price comparisons </p>\n  </li>\n  <li>\n    <p>work towards improved transparency and visibility on microbusiness tariffs, recognising the particular difficulties microbusinesses face in switching providers</p>\n  </li>\n</ul>\n\n<h5 id=\"science-and-innovation\">Science and innovation</h5>\n\n<p>Regius Professorships – The government will introduce new Regius Professorships in order to recognise scientific excellence in universities across the UK. The competition will be launched later this year, with a view to making awards to celebrate the Queen’s 90th birthday.</p>\n\n<p>Digital Economy Centres – The government will invest £23 million in Next Stage Digital Economy Centres. This investment at 6 sites (UCL, Swansea, Newcastle, Nottingham, York and Bath), has leveraged £22 million of additional funding. </p>\n\n<p>Regional science and innovation audits – The government will work with universities, LEPs, cities, and businesses to map science and innovation strengths and identify potential areas of strategic focus for different regions. </p>\n\n<h5 id=\"education-and-skills\">Education and skills</h5>\n\n<p>Childcare – From September 2017, the government will extend the free childcare entitlement to 30 hours a week for working parents of 3 and 4 year olds. (6)</p>\n\n<p>Apprenticeships levy – The government will introduce a levy on large UK employers to increase the number of apprenticeship starts. In England, employers will be able to access this funding for apprenticeship training. Details including rates and implementation will be set out in the Spending Review. </p>\n\n<p>Student maintenance – Maintenance loan support will rise for students from low and middle income backgrounds up to £8,200 a year studying away from home, outside London. From the 2016-17 academic year, maintenance grants will be replaced with maintenance loans for new students from England, paid back only when their earnings exceed £21,000 a year. </p>\n\n<p>Student loans – The government will consult on freezing the loan repayment threshold for the next 5 years and review the discount rate applied to student loans and other transactions to bring it more into line with the government’s long-term cost of borrowing. </p>\n\n<p>Teaching quality – The government will allow institutions offering high teaching quality to increase their tuition fees in line with inflation from 2017-18, and consult on the mechanisms to do this. </p>\n\n<h2 id=\"annex-a-financing\">\n<span class=\"number\">7. </span>Annex A: Financing</h2>\n\n<p>This annex sets out revisions to the government’s financing plans for 2015-16, which were previously updated on 23 April 2015. Further details of the revised remit for 2015-16, including progress against the remit to date, can be found on the Debt Management Office’s (<abbr title=\"Debt Management Office\">DMO</abbr>) website at www.dmo.gov.uk. The government’s debt management framework remains as set out in the Debt and reserves management report 2015-16.</p>\n\n<h3 id=\"financing-arithmetic\">\n<span class=\"number\">7.1 </span>Financing arithmetic</h3>\n\n<p>As set out in Chapter 4 of the Office for Budget Responsibility’s (<abbr title=\"Office for Budget Responsibility\">OBR</abbr>) July 2015 ‘Economic and fiscal outlook’ (<abbr title=\"Economic and fiscal outlook\">EFO</abbr>), the forecast for the 2015-16 central government net cash requirement (excluding <abbr title=\"Northern Rock Asset Management\">NRAM</abbr> plc, Bradford and Bingley and Network Rail) (<abbr title=\"Central government net cash requirement\">CGNCR</abbr> (ex <abbr title=\"Northern Rock Asset Management\">NRAM</abbr>, <abbr title=\"Bradford and Bingley plc\">B&amp;B</abbr> and <abbr title=\"Network Rail\">NR</abbr>)) is £71.6 billion. This measure of the government’s cash requirement is used in the financing arithmetic as it reflects the forecast cash requirement of the Exchequer. The relationship between public sector net borrowing and the <abbr title=\"Central government net cash requirement\">CGNCR</abbr> (ex <abbr title=\"Northern Rock Asset Management\">NRAM</abbr>, <abbr title=\"Bradford and Bingley plc\">B&amp;B</abbr> and <abbr title=\"Network Rail\">NR</abbr>) is set out in the <abbr title=\"Office for Budget Responsibility\">OBR</abbr>’s July 2015 <abbr title=\"Economic and fiscal outlook\">EFO</abbr>.</p>\n\n<p>The net financing requirement (<abbr title=\"Net Financing Requirement\">NFR</abbr>) comprises the <abbr title=\"Central government net cash requirement\">CGNCR</abbr> (ex <abbr title=\"Northern Rock Asset Management\">NRAM</abbr>, <abbr title=\"Bradford and Bingley plc\">B&amp;B</abbr> and <abbr title=\"Network Rail\">NR</abbr>) plus any financing for gilt redemptions, planned financing for the reserves and other adjustments, less the net contribution to financing from National Savings and Investments (<abbr title=\"National Savings and Investments\">NS&amp;I</abbr>) and any other in-year contributions to financing. </p>\n\n<p>The <abbr title=\"Net Financing Requirement\">NFR</abbr> for 2015-16 is projected to be £123.9 billion, a reduction of £14.0 billion relative to that anticipated in April 2015. The change solely reflects the reduction in the <abbr title=\"Office for Budget Responsibility\">OBR</abbr>’s forecast for the <abbr title=\"Central government net cash requirement\">CGNCR</abbr> (ex <abbr title=\"Northern Rock Asset Management\">NRAM</abbr>, <abbr title=\"Bradford and Bingley plc\">B&amp;B</abbr> and <abbr title=\"Network Rail\">NR</abbr>) of £14.0 billion to £71.6 billion, arising from:</p>\n\n<p>• reductions in public sector net borrowing for 2015-16</p>\n\n<p>• income from asset sales including Lloyds, <abbr title=\"Royal Bank of Scotland\">RBS</abbr> and Royal Mail</p>\n\n<p>The majority of the reduction to the <abbr title=\"Net Financing Requirement\">NFR</abbr> will be accommodated by a change in the planned end-year stock of Treasury bills. There will be a net reduction in the Treasury bill stock of £10.5 billion relative to the previously planned stock of £72.0 billion, taking the planned end‑March 2016 Treasury bill stock to £61.5 billion.</p>\n\n<p>Planned gilt sales in 2015-16 will be reduced by £3.5 billion to £127.4 billion. This will be accommodated through a reduction in planned average auction sizes. The updated financing arithmetic is set out in Table A.1.</p>\n\n<h3 id=\"gilt-issuance-by-maturity-type-and-method\">\n<span class=\"number\">7.2 </span>Gilt issuance by maturity, type and method</h3>\n\n<p>Auctions will remain the government’s primary method of gilt issuance. In 2015-16, it is anticipated that:</p>\n\n<p>• £99.2 billion (77.9% of total issuance) will be issued by auction</p>\n\n<p>• £24.5 billion (19.2% of total issuance) will be issued by syndication</p>\n\n<p>In addition:</p>\n\n<ul>\n  <li>\n    <p>£1.0 billion (0.8% of total issuance) has been issued by mini-tender</p>\n  </li>\n  <li>\n    <p>£2.7 billion (2.1% of total issuance) remains outstanding from an initially unallocated portion of supplementary issuance of £4.0 billion, to be delivered via syndication or mini-tender</p>\n  </li>\n</ul>\n\n<p>The maturity skew of gilt issuance by auction and syndication was previously set out in April 2015. This skew will remain broadly unchanged:</p>\n\n<ul>\n  <li>\n    <p>short maturity conventional gilt issuance by auction will fall by £0.9 billion to £32.3 billion (25.4% of total issuance)</p>\n  </li>\n  <li>\n    <p>medium maturity conventional gilt issuance by auction will fall by £0.8 billion to £25.4 billion (19.9% of total issuance)</p>\n  </li>\n  <li>\n    <p>long maturity conventional gilt issuance by auction will fall by £0.9 billion, however an additional £1.0 billion was allocated to long maturity conventional gilts via a mini-tender in June 2015. Taking this into account, long maturity conventional issuance will now increase by £0.1 billion to £36.8 billion (28.9% of total issuance)</p>\n  </li>\n  <li>\n    <p>index-linked gilt issuance by auction will fall by £0.9 billion, however an additional £0.3 billion was allocated to index-linked gilts via a syndication in June 2015. Taking this into account, index-linked gilt issuance will now fall by £0.6 billion to £30.2 billion (23.7% of total issuance)</p>\n  </li>\n</ul>\n\n<h3 id=\"reserves\">\n<span class=\"number\">7.3 </span>Reserves</h3>\n\n<p>The financing arithmetic provides for £5.3 billion of sterling financing for the Official Reserves in 2015-16, as set out in the Revision to the <abbr title=\"Debt Management Office\">DMO</abbr>’s Financing Remit 2015-16, 23 April 2015. This is £0.7 billion less than planned at March Budget 2015, reflecting an offsetting increase in financing in 2014-15 due to increased investments in reserve assets being brought forward at the end of the 2014-15 financial year. </p>\n\n<p>The government is planning on the basis of sterling financing for the Official Reserves of £6.0 billion per year on average, over the 4 years from 2016-17 up to, and including, 2019‑20, thereafter the government has adopted a neutral assumption. This additional financing, announced at Autumn Statement 2014, is intended to ensure that the level of foreign currency reserves held is sufficient for the UK to remain resilient to possible future shocks.</p>\n\n<h3 id=\"national-savings-and-investments\">\n<span class=\"number\">7.4 </span>National Savings and Investments</h3>\n\n<p><abbr title=\"National Savings and Investments\">NS&amp;I</abbr> has a net financing target, which remains at £10.0 billion in 2015-16, within a range of £8.0 to £12.0 billion. This target accommodates sales of <abbr title=\"National Savings and Investments\">NS&amp;I</abbr>’s market-leading bonds for people aged 65 and over (the ‘65+ bond’) in 2015-16, as well as the increase in the Premium Bond limit from £40,000 to £50,000 from 1 June 2015. </p>\n\n<h4 id=\"table-a1-financing-arithmetic-in-2015-16\">Table A.1: Financing arithmetic in 2015-16</h4>\n\n<table>\n  <thead>\n    <tr>\n      <th>£ billion</th>\n      <th>Apr-15</th>\n      <th>Summer Budget 2015</th>\n    </tr>\n  </thead>\n  <tbody>\n    <tr>\n      <td>\n<abbr title=\"Central government net cash requirement\">CGNCR</abbr> (ex <abbr title=\"Northern Rock Asset Management\">NRAM</abbr>, <abbr title=\"Bradford and Bingley plc\">B&amp;B</abbr> and <abbr title=\"Network Rail\">NR</abbr>)</td>\n      <td>85.6</td>\n      <td>71.6</td>\n    </tr>\n    <tr>\n      <td>Gilt redemptions</td>\n      <td>70.2</td>\n      <td>70.2</td>\n    </tr>\n    <tr>\n      <td>Planned financing for the reserves</td>\n      <td>5.3</td>\n      <td>5.3</td>\n    </tr>\n    <tr>\n      <td>Financing adjustment carried forward from previous financial years</td>\n      <td>-13.1</td>\n      <td>-13.1</td>\n    </tr>\n    <tr>\n      <td>Gross financing requirement</td>\n      <td>148.1</td>\n      <td>134.1</td>\n    </tr>\n    <tr>\n      <td>Less:</td>\n      <td> </td>\n      <td> </td>\n    </tr>\n    <tr>\n      <td>Contribution from National Savings and Investments</td>\n      <td>10.0</td>\n      <td>10.0</td>\n    </tr>\n    <tr>\n      <td>Other financing (1)</td>\n      <td>0.2</td>\n      <td>0.2</td>\n    </tr>\n    <tr>\n      <td>Net financing requirement (<abbr title=\"Net Financing Requirement\">NFR</abbr>) for Debt Management Office (<abbr title=\"Debt Management Office\">DMO</abbr>)</td>\n      <td>137.9</td>\n      <td>123.9</td>\n    </tr>\n    <tr>\n      <td>Financed by:</td>\n      <td> </td>\n      <td> </td>\n    </tr>\n    <tr>\n      <td>1. and fiscal outlook: selected tables</h2>\n\n<p>INSERT LINK TO <abbr title=\"Office for Budget Responsibility\">OBR</abbr>’S REPORT</p>\n\n<div class=\"footnotes\">\n  <ol>\n    <li id=\"fn:1\">\n     "body": "<div class=\"govspeak\"><h2 id=\"proof-of-identity\">Proof of identity</h2>\n\n<p>This list covers forms of identfication accepted by the Bona Vacantia division when dealing with dissolved companies.</p>\n\n<p>Please refer to the Guide for Entitled Blood Relatives to find out what identity documents are accepted in Estates cases.</p>\n\n<h2 id=\"money-laundering-regulations\">Money laundering regulations</h2>\n\n<p>The Money Laundering Regulations 2007 require appropriate identity (ID) evidence to be provided when certain transactions take place. </p>\n\n<p>This checklist sets out the ID evidence needed when the transaction involves a company, or other legal structure.</p>\n\n<p>Below we set out the different types of legal structures and the ID evidence required in each case. </p>\n\n<p>Please select the structure that applies to your organisation and provide the relevant ID evidence requested.</p>\n\n<h2 id=\"proof-of-identity-checklist-for-companies-and-other-legal-structures\">Proof of identity checklist for companies and other legal structures</h2>\n\n<table>\n<thead><tr>\n<th>Legal structure</th>\n      <th>Corporate ID required</th>\n      <th>Individual ID required</th>\n    </tr></thead>\n<tbody>\n<tr>\n<td>A company (including a UK LLP) which is not listed on a regulated market such as the London Stock Exchange</td>\n      <td>copy of certificate of incorporation</td>\n      <td>Identity evidence for a) the individual dealing with the transaction and b) all other individuals or entities with more than 25% of the shares or voting rights in the company</td>\n    </tr>\n<tr>\n<td> </td>\n      <td>copy of filed audited accounts</td>\n      <td> </td>\n    </tr>\n<tr>\n<td> </td>\n      <td>details of current company officers (i.e. directors and company secretary) and shareholders</td>\n      <td> </td>\n    </tr>\n<tr>\n<td>A company (including a UK LLP) which is listed on a regulated market such as the London Stock Exchange</td>\n      <td>copy of a dated page from the website of the relevant stock exchange</td>\n      <td>Identity evidence for a) the individual dealing with the transaction and b) all other individuals who exercise management control</td>\n    </tr>\n<tr>\n<td> </td>\n      <td>photocopy of the listing in a reputable daily newspaper</td>\n      <td> </td>\n    </tr>\n<tr>\n<td>A partnership of non-regulated professionals (except an LLP) with five or less partners</td>\n      <td>none (see the separate checklist for individuals)</td>\n      <td>Identity evidence for a) the individual responsible for the transaction and b) all other individual partners</td>\n    </tr>\n<tr>\n<td>A partnership of non-regulated professionals (except an LLP) with six or more partners</td>\n      <td>name of partnership</td>\n      <td>Identity evidence for a) the partner responsible for the transaction and b) one other partner and c) all other individuals who (directly or indirectly) are entitled to, or control, more than 25% of the capital, profits or voting rights</td>\n    </tr>\n<tr>\n<td> </td>\n      <td>trading address</td>\n      <td> </td>\n    </tr>\n<tr>\n<td> </td>\n      <td>registered address (if any)</td>\n      <td> </td>\n    </tr>\n<tr>\n<td> </td>\n      <td>nature of business</td>\n      <td> </td>\n    </tr>\n<tr>\n<td> </td>\n      <td>recent audited accounts</td>\n      <td> </td>\n    </tr>\n<tr>\n<td> </td>\n      <td>list of all partners</td>\n      <td> </td>\n    </tr>\n<tr>\n<td> </td>\n      <td>list of all those with voting rights indicating their voting stake</td>\n      <td> </td>\n    </tr>\n<tr>\n<td>A partnership of regulated professionals (except an LLP) such as a firm of solicitors</td>\n      <td>entry of details held by a relevant professional body</td>\n      <td>Identity evidence for a) the lead partner, b) one other partner, and c) all other individuals who (directly or indirectly) are entitled to, or control, more than 25% of the capital, profits or voting rights</td>\n    </tr>\n<tr>\n<td>A trust</td>\n      <td>list of trustees</td>\n      <td>Identity evidence for a) the trustee with responsibility for the transaction, and b) one other trustee, and c) all individuals or entities who: 1) have a specific interest in at least 25% of the capital of the trust property; or 2) have control over the trust; or 3) belong to a class of person whose main interest benefits under a trust which does not entirely operate for the benefit of specific individuals</td>\n    </tr>\n<tr>\n<td> </td>\n      <td>list of beneficiaries or class of beneficiaries</td>\n      <td> </td>\n    </tr>\n<tr>\n<td> </td>\n      <td>copy of the trust document</td>\n      <td> </td>\n    </tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Other legal structures set up by law</td>\n      <td>any document which establishes, manages or regulates the structure</td>\n      <td>Identity evidence for all individuals or entities who: 1) are beneficiaries of at least 25% of the property where the individual beneficiaries have been determined; or 2) fall into a class of person whose main interest benefits under the structure where individuals in that class are not determined; or 3) control at least 25% of the structure or of the property under the structure</td>\n    </tr>\n<tr>\n<td> </td>\n      <td>a list of any individuals who benefit (if applicable) or a list of the classes whose main interest is served by the structure</td>\n      <td> </td>\n    </tr>\n</tbody>\n</table><h2 id=\"proof-of-identity-checklist-for-individuals\">Proof of identity checklist for individuals</h2>\n\n<p>You cannot use one form of identification for both name and address.</p>\n\n<p>For example, if you provide your driving licence as proof of your name you must provide another form of identification for your address, such as a utility bill.</p>\n\n<table>\n<thead><tr>\n<th>Proof of name</th>\n      <th>Proof of address</th>\n    </tr></thead>\n<tbody>\n<tr>\n<td>Current signed passport</td>\n      <td>Utility bill issued within the last three months</td>\n    </tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Original birth certificate (UK birth certificate issued within 12 months of the date of birth in full form including those issued by UK authorities overseas such as Embassies High Commissions and HM Forces)</td>\n      <td>Local authority council tax bill for the current council tax year</td>\n    </tr>\n<tr>\n<td>EEA member state identity card (which can also be used as evidence of address if it carries this)</td>\n      <td>Current UK driving licence (but only if not used for the name evidence)</td>\n    </tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Current UK or EEA photocard driving licence</td>\n      <td>Bank, Building Society or Credit Union statement or passbook</td>\n    </tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Full old-style driving licence</td>\n      <td>Original mortgage statement from a recognised lender issued for the last full year</td>\n    </tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Photographic registration cards for self-employed individuals in the construction industry -CIS4</td>\n      <td>Solicitors letter confirming recent house purchase or land registry confirmation of address</td>\n    </tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Benefit book or original notification letter from Benefits Agency</td>\n      <td>Council or housing association rent card or tenancy agreement for the current year</td>\n    </tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Firearms or shotgun certificate</td>\n      <td>Benefit book or original notification letter from Benefits Agency (but not if used as proof of name)</td>\n    </tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Residence permit issued by the Home Office to EEA nationals on sight of own country passport</td>\n      <td>Inland Revenue self-assessment or tax demand</td>\n    </tr>\n<tr>\n<td>National identity card bearing a photograph of the applicant</td>\n      <td>Electoral Register entry</td>\n    </tr>\n<tr>\n<td> </td>\n      <td>NHS Medical card</td>\n    </tr>\n</tbody>\n</table><h3 id=\"documents-we-will-not-accept-include-but-are-not-limited-to\">Documents we will not accept include, but are not limited to</h3>\n\n<ul>\n<li>Provisional driving licence</li>\n  <li>Mobile phone bills</li>\n  <li>Credit card statements</li>\n</ul></div>",

{
  "content_id": "1d0ba5bd-8a0a-41a7-950a-c7b819da6336",
  "base_path": "/government/publications/canada-united-kingdom-joint-declaration/canada-united-kingdom-joint-declaration",
  "details": {
    "body": "<div class=\"govspeak\"><p>We, the Prime Ministers of Canada and of the United Kingdom of Great Britain and Northern Ireland, met in Ottawa on September 22, 2011, and have together endorsed this second Joint Declaration between our two countries.</p>\n\n<p>Our meeting today reinvigorates our strategic partnership. The bond between our countries has been forged, in peace and war, notably through two World Wars, and in almost every major conflict for more than a century, including in Afghanistan and Libya. Together, we have prevailed in the face of adversity and challenge, fighting side by side against tyranny and in defence of freedom.</p>\n\n<p>Our common history, our tradition of parliamentary democracy, our shared values, and our partnership on global issues is what binds us together. We have contributed to our mutual development as prosperous and democratic nations—and we stand together as the only two countries that are members of NATO, the G8, the G20 and the Commonwealth. </p>\n\n<p>Today, our two countries jointly face two major challenges in particular: confronting global economic uncertainty and volatility; and supporting the people of the Middle East and North Africa, who are seeking to build inclusive and stable societies, underpinned by democracy, human rights and the rule of law. </p>\n\n<p>As we move forward in addressing these and other challenges, we commit to renewing our bilateral relationship. To this end, over the coming months we will focus on prosperity, security and development cooperation. </p>\n\n<h3 id=\"increasing-economic-growth-trade-and-innovation\">\n<span class=\"number\">0.1 </span>Increasing Economic Growth, Trade and Innovation</h3>\n\n<p>We will work together and through wider cooperation in the G20 to safeguard our mutual prosperity. We will rigorously promote global efforts to ensure strong, sustainable and balanced growth, sound fiscal management, healthy financial sectors and regulatory systems, open markets and productivity-enhancing structural reforms. Our aim is to improve global economic conditions so that enhanced international trade and investment can thrive.</p>\n\n<p>As an important part of this endeavour, we will seek an ambitious and mutually successful outcome to the negotiation of the Canada-EU Comprehensive Economic and Trade Agreement (CETA). This will result in economic growth for both countries, by stimulating competition, increasing trade, expanding market access and promoting joint investment and innovation. </p>\n\n<p>We look forward to concluding a joint innovation statement leveraging existing resources to facilitate late-stage research collaborations, stimulate commercialisation partnerships, and foster an entrepreneurial community between our countries in order to drive economic growth and address global challenges. </p>\n\n<p>In order to fully realise the inherent power of cyberspace to enhance global economic growth, we will pursue common approaches to cyber security that ensures we develop policies and responses that are fully compatible and mutually reinforcing.</p>\n\n<p>Exploiting the fact that Canada and the UK are global leaders in health research, including regenerative medicine and cell therapy, we will use existing initiatives and mechanisms to foster collaboration, facilitating the translation of our advanced knowledge into life-changing therapies that will benefit our patients, healthcare institutions and industries.</p>\n\n<p>We will encourage the development of technology systems necessary for commercial-scale electricity production from marine energy. We plan to lead the world in moving forward from pilot wave and tidal energy devices to exploring actual power generation stations connected to our respective electricity grids.</p>\n\n<h3 id=\"securing-our-countries\">\n<span class=\"number\">0.2 </span>Securing our Countries</h3>\n\n<p>We will continue to work with Afghan and international partners to help build a more viable country that is better governed, more stable and secure, and never again a safe haven for terrorists. Through the training of Afghan National Security Forces (ANSF), regional diplomacy, and development assistance, we are working to help enable the transition of security in Afghanistan to the ANSF by the end of 2014.</p>\n\n<p>We will create greater interoperability between our defence forces and deepen cooperation on procurement and capabilities, to be enabled in part by a Memorandum of Understanding (MoU) on Defence Material Cooperation, existing MoUs and the ‘Partners in Defence’ dialogue, which will draw on the lessons of current and recent national and NATO-led operations. </p>\n\n<p>We will strengthen our counter-terrorism collaboration, in particular in the Horn of Africa, the Sahel and South Asia, including our efforts to tackle terrorist finance activity in third countries. We will advance shared objectives on migration, including through the Five Country Conference on biometric and other information sharing and service delivery partnerships.</p>\n\n<p>Building on the excellent relationship following evacuations of our nationals from Libya and Egypt this year, we will improve cooperation on consular services through joint contingency planning in third countries, and through staff exchanges between our Crisis Centres.</p>\n\n<h3 id=\"promoting-our-shared-values\">\n<span class=\"number\">0.3 </span>Promoting our Shared Values</h3>\n\n<p>Our two militaries have fought side by side to support the will and ambitions of peoples who could not defend themselves. We have successfully supported and defended the right of the Libyan people to choose their own future. We will continue to work closely with the National Transitional Council, recognised by us as the legitimate government authority in Libya, in postconflict stabilisation and the establishment of democracy.</p>\n\n<p>We will also continue to work together, and with our regional and international partners, to support and sustain the democratic reforms underway in the Middle East and North Africa, which are helping build more stable and inclusive societies, underpinned by democratic governance, respect for human rights, freedom of religion, the rule of law, and economies that can respond to the basic needs and aspirations of citizens. </p>\n\n<p>We will work towards a reinvigorated Commonwealth, primarily focusing on its core competency of promoting democracy, good governance, human rights, including freedom of religion, and the rule of law: and by working to collaborate on the adoption and implementation of the recommendations of the Eminent Persons Group report. </p>\n\n<p>We will protect the most vulnerable by working to meet the Millennium Development Goals through development cooperation. We will use effective, results-based development assistance to tackle conflict, ensure food security, foster sustainable economic growth, empower women and protect the health of mothers and children. </p>\n\n<p>We will increase the number of participants in our Youth Mobility programmes, ensuring we foster the next generation’s links between our countries.</p>\n\n<h3 id=\"strengthening-our-partnership-for-results\">\n<span class=\"number\">0.4 </span>Strengthening our Partnership for Results</h3>\n\n<p>We commit ourselves and our governments to achieve what we have set out in this declaration to collaborate on our commerce, foreign policy, defence, security, development and intelligence relationship.</p>\n\n<p>We ask Ministers to meet each year to review and report on progress, and to renew objectives for deepening the relationship. This will thus remain a living document, responsive to evolving events, challenges and opportunities.</p>\n\n<p>Endorsed in Ottawa this 22nd day of September, 2011.</p>\n\n<p>The Rt. Hon. Stephen Harper MP \nPrime Minister of Canada</p>\n\n<p>The Rt. Hon. David Cameron MP\nPrime Minister of the United Kingdom\nof Great Britain and Northern Ireland</p></div>",

    "body": "<div class=\"govspeak\">\n<aside class=\"stat-headline\">\n<p><em>£6bn</em>\nTotal Departmental Expenditure Limit (<abbr title=\"Departmental Expenditure Limit\">DEL</abbr>) in financial year 2015 to 2016</p>\n</aside>\n\n<p>This includes £5.8 billion Resource <abbr title=\"Departmental Expenditure Limit\">DEL</abbr> and £0.2 billion Capital <abbr title=\"Departmental Expenditure Limit\">DEL</abbr>. In addition, <abbr title=\"Department for Work and Pensions\">DWP</abbr> Annually Managed Expenditure (<abbr title=\"Annually Managed Expenditure\">AME</abbr>) in financial year 2015 to 2016 is £170.5 billion, as forecast by the Office for Budget Responsibility. </p>\n\n<p>Source: <a href=\"/government/topical-events/autumn-statement-and-spending-review-2015\">Spending Review and Autumn Statement 2015</a></p>\n\n<p>Source: <a rel=\"external\" href=\"http://cdn.budgetresponsibility.independent.gov.uk/EFO_November__2015.pdf\">Office for Budget Responsibility Economic and Fiscal Outlook 2015</a></p>\n\n<h2 id=\"vision\">Vision</h2>\n\n<p>Everything we do in the Department for Work and Pensions is about providing security, extending opportunity, and giving people the support they need to transform their lives.</p>\n\n<p>We are helping the most vulnerable people in our society by addressing the root causes of disadvantage and supporting them to turn their lives around. </p>\n\n<p>We are ensuring that everyone who is able to work is given all the support they need to do so, while those who cannot are - quite rightly - protected.</p>\n\n<p>Through Universal Credit we are delivering a benefit system that provides the right incentives, ensures work always pays, and which supports people both to get a job and then to progress in employment. </p>\n\n<p>We are giving people greater security, choice and dignity in retirement with a safe and sustainable state pension, and the independence of a well earned private pension.</p>\n\n<p><a href=\"/government/organisations/department-for-work-pensions\">Our ministers and management</a></p>\n\n<h2 id=\"objectives\">Objectives</h2>\n\n<ol>\n  <li>\n    <p><a href=\"/government/publications/dwp-single-departmental-plan-2015-to-2020#run-an-effective-welfare-system-that-enables-people-to-achieve-financial-independence-by-providing-assistance-and-guidance-into-employment\">Run an effective welfare system that enables people to achieve financial independence by providing assistance and guidance into employment</a></p>\n  </li>\n  <li>\n    <p><a href=\"/government/publications/dwp-single-departmental-plan-2015-to-2020#increase-saving-for-and-security-in-later-life\">Increase saving for, and security in, later life</a></p>\n  </li>\n  <li>\n    <p><a href=\"/government/publications/dwp-single-departmental-plan-2015-to-2020#create-a-fair-and-affordable-welfare-system-which-improves-the-life-chances-of-children-and-of-adults\">Create a fair and affordable welfare system which improves the life chances of children and of adults</a></p>\n  </li>\n  <li>\n    <p><a href=\"/government/publications/dwp-single-departmental-plan-2015-to-2020#deliver-outstanding-services-to-our-customers-and-claimants\">Deliver outstanding services to our customers and claimants</a></p>\n  </li>\n  <li>\n    <p><a href=\"/government/publications/dwp-single-departmental-plan-2015-to-2020#transforming-the-way-we-deliver-our-services-to-reduce-costs-and-increas-efficiency\">Delivering Efficiently: transforming the way we deliver our services to reduce costs and increase efficiency</a></p>\n  </li>\n</ol>\n\n<p><a href=\"/government/publications/permanent-secretaries-objectives-2015-to-2016\">Our Permanent Secretary’s objectives</a></p>\n\n<p>Progress against this plan will be measured in the Mid Year Report to Parliament and Annual Report and Accounts. </p>\n\n<h2 id=\"run-an-effective-welfare-system-that-enables-people-to-achieve-financial-independence-by-providing-assistance-and-guidance-into-employment\">\n<span class=\"number\">1. </span> Run an effective welfare system that enables people to achieve financial independence by providing assistance and guidance into employment</h2>\n\n<p>Lead minister: <a href=\"/government/people/priti-patel\">Rt Hon Priti Patel MP, Minister of State for Employment</a></p>\n\n<p>Lead official: <a href=\"/government/people/jeremy-moore\">Jeremy Moore, Director General, Strategy, Policy and Analysis</a></p>\n\n<h3 id=\"what-dwp-is-doing\">\n<span class=\"number\">1.1 </span> What <abbr title=\"Department for Work and Pensions\">DWP</abbr> is doing</h3>\n\n<p>We are transforming people’s life chances by supporting them to become sustainably employed and increase their earnings. This is key to our ambition to have the highest employment rate in the G7. \nWe are pursuing this by:</p>\n\n<ul>\n  <li>continuing to roll out <a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/government/publications/universal-credit-and-other-benefits-quick-guide\">Universal Credit</a> through to financial year 2020 to 2021 and extending job search conditionality to a further 1.3 million claimants to ensure that work always pays  </li>\n  <li>continuing to provide a range of employment support through Jobcentre Plus, the Work Programme (until 2017) and the new Work and Health Programme from 2017</li>\n  <li>supporting people to become self-employed (New Enterprise Allowance)</li>\n  <li>offering working families on Universal Credit support of up to 85% of their eligible childcare costs (where the lone parent or both parents in a couple are in work)</li>\n  <li>helping parents understand the government’s childcare offer </li>\n</ul>\n\n<p>We will make progress towards our ambition to halve the disability employment gap by supporting disabled people and people with long term health conditions to get in and stay in employment. \nWe are doing this by:</p>\n\n<ul>\n  <li>reforming the welfare system to support people with disabilities and health conditions into work, whilst protecting the most vulnerable. We will be publishing a White Paper in 2016 that will set out plans to improve support for people with health conditions and disabilities, including exploring the roles of employers, and promoting integration across health and employment </li>\n  <li>continuing to provide specialist provision for people with health conditions and disabilities within Jobcentre Plus, Work Programme and Work Choice until 2017</li>\n  <li>introducing a new Work and Health programme from 2017, which we will work with local partners to deliver, which will provide specialist support for claimants with health conditions and disabilities and those unemployed for over 2 years</li>\n  <li>providing a more personalised and improved service offer within Universal Credit ensuring that work always pays</li>\n  <li>supporting employers to recruit and retain disabled workers through initiatives such as Disability Confident</li>\n  <li>providing in work support for disabled people through Access to Work </li>\n  <li>supporting employees who are off sick from work to return through the <a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/government/collections/fit-for-work-guidance\">Fit for Work</a> service </li>\n  <li>improving access to health treatments including investing an additional £600 million in mental health services</li>\n  <li>improving links between health services and employment support through a Joint Work and Health Unit </li>\n</ul>\n\n<p>We are supporting young people to find work whilst making progress towards our ambition to abolish long term youth unemployment by:</p>\n\n<ul>\n  <li>introducing Youth Obligation through Universal Credit from 2017 which will include intensive support for those 18 to 21 year olds who we expect to look for work from when they first claim requiring those still out of work after 6 months to apply for an apprenticeship, a traineeship, gain work-base skills or take up a work placement </li>\n  <li>introducing Jobcentre Plus support into schools in England to supplement careers advice and provide routes into apprenticeships, <a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/government/statistics/work-experience\">work experience and sector-based work academy places</a>\n</li>\n</ul>\n\n<p>We are supporting the Prime Minister’s ambition to increase the number of workers from ethnic minority backgrounds in employment by 20% by 2020, by:</p>\n\n<ul>\n  <li>identifying and sharing good practice in jobcentres to support people from ethnic minority backgrounds into employment </li>\n  <li>working with exemplar employers to learn how they encourage diversity in their organisations</li>\n</ul>\n\n<p>We are supporting increased labour supply and retirement incomes through employer-led initiatives on fuller working lives, ensuring older people do not leave the labour market early through avoidable medical retirement, inability to balance caring responsibilities with employment, or the need to re-skill or change occupations.</p>\n\n<h3 id=\"how-dwp-is-doing\">\n<span class=\"number\">1.2 </span> How <abbr title=\"Department for Work and Pensions\">DWP</abbr> is doing</h3>\n\n<aside class=\"stat-headline\">\n<p>UK employment rate\n<em>74.1%</em>\nbetween October and December 2015</p>\n</aside>\n\n<p>The overall UK employment rate reached a new record high of 74.1% between October and December 2015, up 3.9 percentage points since 2010 and well above the pre-recession peak of 73%.</p>\n\n<p>Source: <a rel=\"external\" href=\"http://www.ons.gov.uk/ons/rel/lms/labour-market-statistics/index.html\">Labour Market Statistics</a> published by the Office for National Statistics.</p>\n\n<aside class=\"stat-headline\">\n<p>Employment rate for disabled people \n<em>46.7%</em>\nbetween October and December 2015</p>\n</aside>\n\n<p>The employment rate for disabled people between October and December 2015 was 46.7%, up from 45.46% in the same quarter in 2014. A change in the current definition of disability means the current rate cannot be directly compared to data before 2013.</p>\n\n<p>Source: <a rel=\"external\" href=\"http://www.ons.gov.uk/ons/about-ons/get-involved/taking-part-in-a-survey/information-for-households/a-to-z-of-household-and-individual-surveys/labour-force-survey/index.html\">Labour Force Survey</a> published by the Office for National Statistics</p>\n\n<aside class=\"stat-headline\">\n<p>Percentage of young people not in full-time education in employment\n<em>75.8%</em>\nbetween October and December 2015</p>\n</aside>\n\n<p>In October to December 2015 75.8% of young people not in full time education were in employment compared to 69.0% in February to April 2010. The proportion of the total 18 to 24 population who are not in full-time education and are unemployed is 6.5%.</p>\n\n<p>Source: <a rel=\"external\" href=\"http://www.ons.gov.uk/ons/about-ons/get-involved/taking-part-in-a-survey/information-for-households/a-to-z-of-household-and-individual-surveys/labour-force-survey/index.html\">Labour Force Survey</a> published by the Office for National Statistics.</p>\n\n<aside class=\"stat-headline\">\n<p>Number of people on key out-of-work benefits\n<em>3.8m</em>\nin August 2015</p>\n</aside>\n\n<p>In August 2015 there were 3.8 million people on a key out of work benefit compared to 4.9 million in 2010. </p>\n\n<p>Source: <a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/government/statistics/work-and-pensions-longitudinal-study\">Work and Pensions Longitudinal Study</a> and ONS Claimant Count.</p>\n\n<h2 id=\"increase-saving-for-and-security-in-later-life\">\n<span class=\"number\">2. </span> Increase saving for, and security in, later life</h2>\n\n<p>Lead minister: <a href=\"/government/people/ros-altmann\">Baroness Altmann CBE, Minister of State for Pensions</a></p>\n\n<p>Lead official: <a href=\"/government/people/jeremy-moore\">Jeremy Moore, Director General, Strategy, Policy and Analysis</a></p>\n\n<h3 id=\"what-dwp-is-doing-1\">\n<span class=\"number\">2.1 </span> What <abbr title=\"Department for Work and Pensions\">DWP</abbr> is doing</h3>\n\n<p>We are providing greater security, choice and dignity for people in retirement, while also ensuring the system is sustainable for the future.</p>\n\n<p>To give everybody the confidence that they will receive a decent state pension, we are:</p>\n\n<ul>\n  <li>putting the State Pension system on a fair and sustainable basis, giving people greater understanding and confidence through the introduction of the <a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/new-state-pension\">new State Pension</a>\n</li>\n  <li>continuing to support current pensioners through the triple lock, and by protecting universal pensioner benefits in the UK such as Winter Fuel Payment</li>\n  <li>giving those not eligible for the new State Pension the opportunity to ensure a decent retirement income through State Pension top-up </li>\n  <li>giving people security in their retirement income by paying State Pension and other pensioner benefits (£94.5 billion in financial year 2014 to 2015)</li>\n</ul>\n\n<p>We are helping working people save for a private pension and giving them the freedom to access their pension pots in the best way for them by:</p>\n\n<ul>\n  <li>completing the roll out of <a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/government/publications/2010-to-2015-government-policy-automatic-enrolment-in-workplace-pensions\">Automatic Enrolment</a> to small and micro businesses, giving all eligible employees the opportunity to enrol into a workplace pension and save for their retirement</li>\n  <li>removing the restrictions on how people access their private pension pots, giving people aged 55 and over greater choice in how to spend their well-earned savings</li>\n  <li>protecting savers by working with HM Treasury, Pension Wise, the <a rel=\"external\" href=\"http://www.thepensionsregulator.gov.uk/\">Pensions Regulator</a> and <a rel=\"external\" href=\"http://www.fca.org.uk/\">Financial Conduct Authority</a> to monitor the products, charges and processes affecting individuals accessing their private savings</li>\n  <li>giving savers the confidence to save and access their pension pots by providing more information on pensions through <a rel=\"external\" href=\"http://www.pensionsadvisoryservice.org.uk/\">the Pensions Advisory Service,</a> <a rel=\"external\" href=\"https://www.pensionwise.gov.uk/\">Pension Wise</a>, pension forecasts and <a rel=\"external\" href=\"https://www2.dwp.gov.uk/tps-directgov/en/contact-tps/pension-tracing-form.asp\">pensions tracing</a> </li>\n  <li>working with employers and stakeholders to give people the opportunity to work and to save for as long as they wish</li>\n</ul>\n\n<h3 id=\"how-dwp-is-doing-1\">\n<span class=\"number\">2.2 </span> How <abbr title=\"Department for Work and Pensions\">DWP</abbr> is doing</h3>\n\n<aside class=\"stat-headline\">\n<p>Pension scheme membership\n<em>13.9m</em>\neligible employees in a pension scheme sponsored by their employer, in 2014</p>\n</aside>\n\n<p>This represents a 2.5 million improvement from 11.4 million in 2010. </p>\n\n<p>Source:  <a rel=\"external\" href=\"http://www.ons.gov.uk/ons/rel/ashe/annual-survey-of-hours-and-earnings/index.html\">Annual Survey of Hours and Earnings (ASHE).</a> </p>\n\n<aside class=\"stat-headline\">\n<p>Percentage of pensioners with a low income\n<em>14%</em>\nin financial year 2013 to 2014</p>\n</aside>\n\n<p>This rate has remained stable in recent years and at a near historical low. </p>\n\n<p>Source: <a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/government/collections/households-below-average-income-hbai--2\">Households below average Income</a></p>\n\n<h2 id=\"create-a-fair-and-affordable-welfare-system-which-improves-the-life-chances-of-children-and-of-adults\">\n<span class=\"number\">3. </span> Create a fair and affordable welfare system which improves the life chances of children and of adults</h2>\n\n<p>Lead minister: <a href=\"/government/people/iain-duncan-smith\">Rt Hon Iain Duncan Smith MP, Secretary of State for Work and Pensions</a></p>\n\n<p>Lead official: <a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/government/people/jeremy-moore\">Jeremy Moore, Director General, Strategy, Policy and Analysis</a></p>\n\n<h3 id=\"what-dwp-is-doing-2\">\n<span class=\"number\">3.1 </span> What <abbr title=\"Department for Work and Pensions\">DWP</abbr> is doing</h3>\n\n<p>We are managing welfare expenditure by implementing the measures announced in the Budget 2015, to reduce the cost of the welfare system by £12 billion by 2019 to 2020, while protecting the most vulnerable, including:</p>\n\n<ul>\n  <li>lowering the amount of benefits a household can receive out-of-work to £23,000 in Greater London and to £20,000 for residents elsewhere (with exemptions to protect the most vulnerable)</li>\n  <li>ensuring 18 to 21 year olds, who are out of work, no longer have automatic entitlement to support with housing costs from April 2017 (with exemptions to protect the most vulnerable)</li>\n  <li>freezing the rates of working age benefits and tax credits for 4 years from April 2016 (with exemptions to protect the most vulnerable)</li>\n</ul>\n\n<p>We are also:</p>\n\n<ul>\n  <li>taking action to manage expenditure within the welfare cap </li>\n  <li>further reforming welfare rules so that European Union jobseekers can no longer access UK means-tested benefits (from June 2015 we have ended European Union jobseekers’ entitlement to Universal Credit)</li>\n  <li>reducing immigration by cutting the benefits European Union migrants get so we prevent the welfare system acting as a magnet and create a fairer system for people who work hard and play by the rules </li>\n</ul>\n\n<p>We are supporting disabled people to live independently by:</p>\n\n<ul>\n  <li>Replacing Disability Living Allowance with <a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/pip\">Personal Independence Payment</a> (<abbr title=\"Personal Independence Payment\">PIP</abbr>). We have introduced Personal Independence Payment, which is designed to better reflect today’s understanding of disability, particularly on mental health and fluctuating conditions, and to focus support on those in greatest need. Personal Independence Payment is exempt from the benefit freeze over the life of the Parliament and is also exempt from the benefit cap</li>\n  <li>paying disability and carers’ benefits (£23.1 billion in financial year 2014 to 2015)</li>\n</ul>\n\n<p>We are improving the life chances of children and of adults by:</p>\n\n<ul>\n  <li>developing a Life Chances Strategy, which will set out a comprehensive plan to fight disadvantage and extend opportunity so that every child can reach their full potential</li>\n  <li>introducing new life chances measures on worklessness and educational attainment, along with other measures of the root causes of poverty including, family stability, drug and alcohol dependency and financial stability </li>\n  <li>encouraging family stability, by improving the availability of support for couples (we will spend over £70 million this Parliament, exceeding the manifesto commitment to invest at least £7.5 million in relationship support), developing a significantly expanded parenting programme, and implementing reforms to the Child Maintenance Service to encourage family based arrangements where appropriate</li>\n</ul>\n\n<p>We are working closely with all the nations within the UK, in particular where areas of policy are closely linked, and particularly with the Scottish government on how newly devolved powers will work in practice, as part of this we are:</p>\n\n<ul>\n  <li>working with the Scotland Office to implement recommendations of the Smith Commission relating to <abbr title=\"Department for Work and Pensions\">DWP</abbr> policy through delivery of the Scotland Bill, which includes devolving powers to the Scottish government to deliver a range of benefits and employment support</li>\n  <li>supporting the principle of localism, working with local authorities, community groups and charities to join up delivery</li>\n</ul>\n\n<h3 id=\"how-dwp-is-doing-2\">\n<span class=\"number\">3.2 </span> How <abbr title=\"Department for Work and Pensions\">DWP</abbr> is doing</h3>\n\n<h3 id=\"forecast-welfare-spending-within-the-welfare-cap\">Forecast welfare spending within the welfare cap</h3>\n\n<p>As required under the Charter for Budget Responsibility, the welfare cap was reset for this Parliament at the July 2015 Budget, where the government set it at the Office for Budget Responsibility’s post-measures forecast. This locked in a reduction in the level of the cap compared with Autumn Statement 2014 that reached £16.3 billion by financial year 2019 to 2020. </p>\n\n<p>The Office for Budget Responsibility assessment at Autumn Statement 2015 was that the welfare cap will be met in financial year 2019 to 2020 and financial year 2020 to 2021, although not in earlier years. This was because the government gave families longer to adjust to the higher wage, lower tax and lower welfare society. </p>\n\n<p>In financial year 2016 to 2017, more than a third of spending within the welfare cap will be administered by other government departments. This share will gradually reduce as Universal Credit (administered by <abbr title=\"Department for Work and Pensions\">DWP</abbr>) replaces tax credits (administered by HM Revenue and Customs), though around 14% of capped spending will continue to be outside direct Department for Work and Pensions control in the longer term. </p>\n\n<aside class=\"stat-headline\">\n<p>Percentage of children living in workless households\n<em>11.8%</em>\nin April to June 2015</p>\n</aside>\n\n<p>In April to June 2015 11.8% of children were living in a workless household an improvement from 16.2% in the same quarter in 2010. </p>\n\n<p>Source: <a rel=\"external\" href=\"http://www.ons.gov.uk/ons/rel/lmac/working-and-workless-households/index.html\">The Household Labour Force Survey.</a></p>\n\n<h2 id=\"deliver-outstanding-services-to-our-customers-and-claimants\">\n<span class=\"number\">4. </span> Deliver outstanding services to our customers and claimants</h2>\n\n<p>Lead minister: <a href=\"/government/people/lord-freud\">Lord Freud, Minister of State for Welfare Reform</a></p>\n\n<p>Lead official: <a href=\"/government/people/noel-shanahan\">Noel Shanahan, Director General, Operations</a></p>\n\n<h3 id=\"what-dwp-is-doing-3\">\n<span class=\"number\">4.1 </span> What <abbr title=\"Department for Work and Pensions\">DWP</abbr> is doing</h3>\n\n<p>We deliver essential services for welfare, pensions and child maintenance. We are continually seeking to deliver outstanding services by:</p>\n\n<ul>\n  <li>streamlining our business processes and simplifying our communications</li>\n  <li>improving the timeliness and accuracy of benefit processing</li>\n  <li>ensuring our digital technology and data services are easy to use, stable and secure</li>\n  <li>ensuring we have an engaged and committed workforce </li>\n</ul>\n\n<h3 id=\"how-dwp-is-doing-3\">\n<span class=\"number\">4.2 </span> How <abbr title=\"Department for Work and Pensions\">DWP</abbr> is doing</h3>\n\n<aside class=\"stat-headline\">\n<p>Customer and claimant satisfaction of <abbr title=\"Department for Work and Pensions\">DWP</abbr> services (%)\n<em>82%</em>\noverall customer satisfaction rating, in financial year 2014 to 2015</p>\n</aside>\n\n<p>Latest data shows we achieved an overall customer satisfaction rating of 82% in financial year 2014 to 2015, which is similar to the 83% achieved in 2011 (the year of the first pan departmental survey). </p>\n\n<p>Source: Claimant Service and Experience Survey <a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/government/publications/jobcentre-plus-customer-survey-2011rr775\">2011,</a> <a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/government/publications/dwp-claimant-service-and-experience-survey-2012-rr-831\">2012,</a> <a href=\"government/admin/publications/402570\">2013,</a> <a href=\"/government/publications/dwp-claimant-service-and-experience-survey-2014-to-2015\">2014 to 2015.</a></p>\n\n<aside class=\"stat-headline\">\n<p>Benefits processed within planned timescales \n<em>90%</em>\nof key out of work benefits processed within agreed timescales, in financial year 2014 to 2015</p>\n</aside>\n\n<p>In financial year 2014 to 2015 89.7% of key out of work benefits were processed within financial year 2014 to 2015 agreed timescales, an improvement from financial year 2010 to 2011 when 69.2% of key out of work benefits were processed within timescales agreed for financial year 2014 to 2015. </p>\n\n<p>Source: <abbr title=\"Department for Work and Pensions\">DWP</abbr> Management Information Systems Programme. </p>\n\n<aside class=\"stat-headline\">\n<p>Net benefit overpayments as a percentage of overall benefit expenditure\n<em>1.2%</em>\n(estimated)</p>\n</aside>\n\n<p>In 2014/15 the estimated level of net overpayments arising from fraud and error, after debt recovered has been offset, was 1.2%, an improvement from 1.7% in financial year 2010 to 2011.</p>\n\n<p>Source: <a href=\"/government/collections/fraud-and-error-in-the-benefit-system\">Fraud and Error in the Benefit System</a></p>\n\n<h2 id=\"delivering-efficiently-transforming-the-way-we-deliver-our-services-to-reduce-costs-and-increase-efficiency\">\n<span class=\"number\">5. </span> Delivering efficiently: transforming the way we deliver our services to reduce costs and increase efficiency</h2>\n\n<p>Lead minister: <a href=\"/government/people/lord-freud\">Lord Freud, Minister of State for Welfare Reform</a></p>\n\n<p>Lead official: <a href=\"/government/people/mike-driver\">Mike Driver, Director General, Finance</a></p>\n\n<h3 id=\"what-dwp-is-doing-4\">What <abbr title=\"Department for Work and Pensions\">DWP</abbr> is doing</h3>\n\n<p>We are committed to ensure value for money for the taxpayer by reducing our operating costs over the Parliament, whilst continuing to improve the efficiency and effectiveness of our services by:</p>\n\n<ul>\n  <li>continuing to redesign our customer services, increasing the use of digital services, streamlining and automating back-office processes  </li>\n  <li>harnessing data and analytics to make better business decisions more quickly </li>\n  <li>establishing more flexible, cost-effective contracts with IT suppliers, including contracts with small and medium sized businesses</li>\n  <li>investing in a smaller and more skilled workforce and building our technology and commercial capability</li>\n  <li>reducing our estate and increasing the number of job centres co-located with partner organisations such as local authorities</li>\n  <li>targeting and reducing spend on contracted employment programmes</li>\n  <li>reducing fraud and error while maximising debt recovery </li>\n  <li>securing efficiencies from our arm’s length bodies</li>\n</ul>\n\n<p>Progress against our ambition to reduce <abbr title=\"Departmental Expenditure Limit\">DEL</abbr> expenditure of 14% in real terms will be published in our Annual Report and Accounts. </p>\n\n<h3 id=\"how-dwp-is-working-collaboratively-across-government\">How <abbr title=\"Department for Work and Pensions\">DWP</abbr> is working collaboratively across government</h3>\n\n<p>We will work collaboratively with Cabinet Office, HM Treasury and other government departments to deliver transformational change in key areas, including:</p>\n\n<ul>\n  <li>developing digital solutions that meet common standards set by the Government Digital Service and utilise cross government platforms wherever this demonstrates the best value money solution for government</li>\n  <li>rationalising our estate using ‘government hubs’ with other departments and local authorities, releasing land for housing where possible, and participating in the development of the new commercial property model</li>\n  <li>delivering savings in our commercial relationships including through spend on common goods and services, in partnership with the Crown Commercial Services. Continuing to build our commercial capability and working with the Crown Commercial Services to deliver the government’s 33% commitment of our spend with small and medium sized enterprises by 2020</li>\n  <li>working in partnership with the Cabinet Office to deliver arm’s length bodies transformation plans and Infrastructure and Projects Authority on major projects, programmes and prioritisation</li>\n</ul>\n\n</div>",
